Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner

Father's Right to Hire Out His Son for Work
Commentary on hiring out a child for work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a father hiring out his male child for work and identify the condition that determines whether nafaqah remains obligatory on the father.

Core Idea
A father may hire out his son only if the son can earn; otherwise nafaqah stays on the father.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn's phrase 'so when this is the case.' It clarifies when a father may hire out his minor son for work and when he must continue providing maintenance. The ruling is based on the child's benefit—learning a trade—and has implications for the nafaqah obligations of other relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What action is being ruled upon? The father hiring out his male child for work or service. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz/mubah).
2
Identify the condition for permissibility
The child must have reached 'hadd al-kasb'—the stage of being capable of earning. This is a condition for the father's right to hire him out.
If the child hasn't reached this stage, the father cannot hire him out and must still provide nafaqah.
3
Identify the consequence when condition is not met
If the child has not yet learned or does not do the work well, then nafaqah remains obligatory on the father. The child's inability to earn properly triggers the father's duty to support.
4
Note the extension to other relatives
Al-Ramli deduces that if the father is not obligated to support a child who can earn, then other mahram relatives are even less obligated. This is a fortiori (min bab al-awla).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإذا كان هذا) أي بلغ حد الكسب . قال في التتارخانية : ولو أراد الأب أن يؤاجرهم أي الذكور في عمل أو أخدمة فله ذلك لأن فيه منفعة للصغير لأنه يتعلم الكسب، أما قبل أن يتعلم أو بعده ولكن لا يحسن العمل فنفقته على الأب اهـ. قال الرملي : وصرح به أيضاً كثير من علمائنا :قال وبه علم أن غير الأب من المحارم لا تجب نفقة القادر على الكسب عليه من باب أولى لأنها لدفع الحاجة وقد اندفعت وصار غنياً بكسبه فلا حاجة إلى إيجابها على الفقير كما هو ظاهر وهي واقعة الفتوى وقد أفتيت فيها بعدم الوجوب اهـ
His statement: 'So when this is the case' i.e., (the child) has reached the age of earning. He said in al-TatarKhaniyya: If the father wants to hire them out, i.e., the males, for work or service, he may do so because there is benefit for the minor as he learns earning. As for before he learns or after but he does not do the work well, then his nafaqah is on the father. Al-Ramli said: Many of our scholars also stated this explicitly. He said: By this it is known that other than the father from among the mahram relatives are not obligated to provide nafaqah for the one capable of earning a fortiori, because it is to remove need, and the need has been removed and he has become wealthy by his earning, so there is no need to obligate it upon the poor person as is apparent, and this is the operative fatwa, and I have given fatwa upon it that it is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'فإذا كان هذا' (so when this is the case). The commentator explains that when a child (specifically a male) has reached the stage of being able to earn a living (بلغ حد الكسب), the father has the right to hire him out for work or service. The rationale is that this benefits the child by teaching him a skill. However, if the child has not yet learned the work or does not perform it well, his maintenance (nafaqah) still falls on the father. Al-Ramli adds that this implies that other mahram relatives are not required to support a child who can earn, because the need is removed. This is the position upon which fatwa is given.

Key Terms
حد الكسب (hadd al-kasb): The age or stage at which a child is capable of earning a living.
إيجار (ijar): Hiring out (here, of a child for work).
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, owed to dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rationale for allowing a father to hire out his male child for work?
A) To relieve the father of nafaqah
B) To benefit the child by teaching him a trade
C) To allow the child to support the family
D) It is always permissible regardless of benefit

Key Takeaway
A father's right to hire out his son for work is conditional on the son's earning capacity; otherwise, the father must provide nafaqah.

Father Cannot Hire Out His Daughter to Non-Mahrams
Commentary on the father's inability to hire out his daughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a father hiring out his daughter and identify the conditions and prohibitions based on mahram and khalwah.

Core Idea
A father may not hire out his daughter to a non-mahram due to the prohibition of khalwah.

In this passage, the commentator Al-Ramli clarifies a ruling about a father's authority over his daughter's labor. While a father can hire out his son when he reaches earning capacity, the daughter is different. The key prohibition is hiring her out to non-mahrams, as it leads to seclusion (khalwah) which is haram. However, if the daughter can work at home or for a mahram, it is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is a father hiring out his daughter. The general ruling is that he does not have the same right as for a son.
The base text says 'وليس له في الأنثى ذلك'.
2
Understand the prohibition's basis
The prohibition is due to khalwah with a non-mahram, which is haram.
The text explicitly says 'لأن الخلوة مع الأجنبية حرام'.
3
Identify exceptions
It is permissible to hire her out to a mahram, or if the work is done at her home.
Al-Khaniyya restricts the prohibition to non-mahram.
4
Analyze nafaqah implications
If she earns enough from permissible work, her nafaqah may come from her earnings; otherwise the father remains responsible.
Al-Ramli discusses the father's obligation if earnings are insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وليس له في الأنثى ذلك قال الرملي : لو استغنت بنحو خياطة وغزل يجب أن تكون نفقتها في كسبها كما هو ظاهر، ولا نقول يجب على الأب مع ذلك إلا إذا كان لا يكفيها فتجب على الأب كفايتها بدفع القدر المعجوز عنه ولم أره لأصحابنا، ولا ينافي ذلك قولهم إذا بلغ حد الكسب للأب يؤجره بخلاف الأنثى لأن الممنوع إيجارها ولا يلزم منه عدم الزامها بحرفة تعلمها اهـ . قلت : حسن ويؤيده أنه في الخانية قيد عدم دفع الأنثى بغير المحرم حيث قال: وإن كان الولد بنتاً لا يملك الأب دفعها إلى غير المحرم لأن الخلوة مع الأجنبية حرام .اهـ فيفيد أنه يؤجرها للمحرم وأنه لو كان المستأجر يدفع لها العمل لتعمل في بيتها كالخياطة ونحوها لا تلزم نفقتها على غيرها لعدم المحظور والله أعلم
His statement: 'And he does not have that for the female.' Al-Ramli said: If she becomes independent through sewing and spinning, then her nafaqah should come from her earnings as is apparent. And we do not say that it is obligatory upon the father unless it does not suffice her, then it is obligatory upon the father to provide her sufficiency by paying the amount she is unable to earn. I have not seen this from our scholars. And this does not contradict their statement that when he reaches earning capacity the father may hire him out, unlike the female, because what is prohibited is hiring her out, and it does not necessitate that she is not required to learn a craft. I say: This is good and it is supported by the fact that in al-Khaniyya, the prohibition of sending the female is restricted to a non-mahram, where it is said: If the child is a female, the father does not have the right to send her to a non-mahram because khalwah with an ajnabiyyah is haram. So it indicates that he may hire her out to a mahram, and that if the hirer gives her the work to do in her own home, like sewing and similar, then her nafaqah is not obligatory upon others due to the absence of prohibition. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'وليس له في الأنثى ذلك' (and he does not have that for the female). The commentator explains that a father cannot hire out his daughter to non-mahrams because of the prohibition of khalwah (seclusion). However, if the daughter earns through work like sewing at home, her income may cover her nafaqah. The father is not relieved of nafaqah unless her earnings suffice. The key distinction is that hiring out a female is prohibited only to non-mahrams; it is permissible for a mahram. Also, if the work can be done in her home, it is allowed.

Key Terms
المحرم (al-mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
الخلوة (al-khalwah): Seclusion between a man and a woman who are not mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a father not hire out his daughter to a non-mahram?
A) Because it is a waste of her time
B) Because it leads to khalwah which is haram
C) Because she is not capable of work
D) Because the father has no authority over her

Key Takeaway
A father may not hire out his daughter to a non-mahram due to the prohibition of khalwah, but hiring to a mahram or work at home is permissible.

Hiring a Wet Nurse at the Mother’s Home
Commentary on the ruling that a wet nurse should be hired to breastfeed at the mother's home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where a wet nurse must breastfeed and explain the disagreement on whether the mother is compelled to accept custody.

Core Idea
The father must provide a wet nurse at the mother’s home because custody is her right and expense is his.

In Hanafi family law, the father is obligated to financially support the child, including hiring a wet nurse if necessary. However, the location of breastfeeding is tied to the mother's custody right. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the default ruling and explores a key disagreement within the school: is the mother compelled to take custody, or is it her choice? Understanding this helps apply the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The matn states that the father hires someone to breastfeed the child at the mother's place. Determine the basic obligation and location.
The commentary emphasizes 'because custody belongs to her'.
2
Examine the rationale
The ruling is based on two factors: custody (right of mother) and nafaqah (expense on father). The location follows custody.
3
Note the restriction in al-Hidayah
Al-Marghinani restricts the ruling to when the mother desires custody, based on the view that she is not compelled.
This is a minority view within the school.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf on compulsion
The three jurists (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the mother is compelled because custody is the child's right. This makes the father's obligation unconditional.
The preferred view is compulsion.
5
Review additional details
The passage from al-Dhakhira addresses the wet nurse's obligations: she is not required to stay in the mother's home unless stipulated. Also, rent for the custody home is generally not obligatory.
These details refine the ruling's application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويستأجر من يرضعه عندها) أي ويستأجر الأب من يرضع الطفل عند الأم لأن الحضانة لها والنفقة عليه أطلقه هنا وقيده في الهداية بإرادة الأم للحضانة وهو مبني على ما صححه من أن الأم لا تجبر عليها لأنها حقها، وعلى ما اختاره الفقهاء الثلاثة من الجبر فليس معلقاً بإرادتها لأنها حق الصبي عليها. وفي الذخيرة: لا يجب على الظئر أن تمكث في بيت الأم إذا لم يشترط عليها ذلك وقت العقد وكان الولد يستغني عن الظئر في تلك الحالة، بل لها أن ترضع وتعود إلى منزلها كما لها أن تحمل الصبي إلى منزلها أو تقول أخرجوه فترضعه عند فناء الدار ثم تدخل الولد على الوالدة إلا أن يشرط عند العقد أن الظئر تكون عند الأم فحينئذ يلزمها الوفاء بذلك الشرط اهـ. وفي الخزانة عن التفاريق : لا تجب في الحضانة أجرة المسكن الذي يحضن فيه الصبي. وقال آخرون : تجب إن كان للصبي مال وإلا فعلى من يجب عليه نفقته اهـ
His statement: 'And he hires someone to breastfeed him at her place' i.e., the father hires someone to breastfeed the child at the mother's home because custody belongs to her and nafaqah is upon him. He made it absolute here and restricted it in al-Hidayah to the mother's desire for custody, which is based on what he corrected that the mother is not compelled to custody because it is her right, and according to what the three jurists chose of compulsion, so it is not conditional upon her desire because it is the right of the child upon her. And in al-Dhakhira: It is not obligatory upon the wet nurse to stay in the mother's home if that was not stipulated at the time of the contract and the child is independent of the wet nurse in that situation. Rather, she may breastfeed and return to her home, just as she may carry the child to her home or say: take him out and I will breastfeed him in the courtyard of the house, then she brings the child in to the mother, unless it was stipulated at the time of the contract that the wet nurse be with the mother, then she must fulfill that condition. And in al-Khazanah from al-Tafariq: The rent for the house in which the child is fostered is not obligatory in custody. And others said: It is obligatory if the child has wealth, otherwise upon the one who is obligated for his nafaqah.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'ويستأجر من يرضعه عندها' (and he hires someone to breastfeed him at her place). It explains that the father must hire a wet nurse to breastfeed the child at the mother's home because the mother has custody (hadanah) and the father bears the expense. There is a difference of opinion: some say the mother is not compelled to accept custody (it is her right), but the three jurists (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that she is compelled because custody is the child's right. The wet nurse is not required to stay in the mother's home unless stipulated. The passage also discusses the rent for the custody home: it is generally not obligatory, but if the child has property, it may be taken from that.

Key Terms
الحضانة (al-hadanah): The right and duty to physically care for and raise a child.
الظئر (al-dhir'): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where must a wet nurse breastfeed the child according to the relied-upon position?
A) At the father's home
B) At the mother's home because she has custody
C) At the wet nurse's own home
D) At a neutral location

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a wet nurse is to breastfeed at the mother’s home because custody belongs to the mother, and the father bears the expense; this rule is affirmed by the majority of Hanafi jurists.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Three Obligatory Child Maintenance Expenses
Breakdown of expenses owed by father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of child expenses owed by the father and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
A father owes three wajib expenses: breastfeeding fee, custody fee, and general maintenance.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq synthesises previous Hanafi works to clarify that the father's maintenance obligations are not a single lump sum but three distinct wajibat. Understanding each category and its evidence is essential for applying the correct rulings in family law cases, especially after divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three expenses
Read the opening lines that explicitly list: ujrat al-rida', ujrat al-hadana, and nafaqat al-walad. Note that the author states 'تجب على الأب ثلاثة'.
These are three separate wajibat, not one combined obligation.
2
Locate the proof for each
The author cites sources: (i) breastfeeding fee is explicitly stated in earlier texts, (ii) custody fee is affirmed by Qari al-Hidayah in his fatwa, (iii) general maintenance is mentioned in the chapter on hiring a wet nurse via al-Zayla'i quoting Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The custody fee proof is a later fatwa, indicating an evolution in Hanafi position.
3
Note the mother's limited duties
The passage explicitly says the mother is only responsible for breastfeeding, preparing food, and washing clothes. All other expenses are on the father.
This clarifies that the mother is not obligated to provide beyond these core services.
4
Understand the breastfeeding duration
The passage mentions three periods: minimum 1.5 years, optimal 2.5 years, and allows weaning before 2 years if the child is independent.
This duration affects calculation of fees if no mutual agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيء آخر كما هو المشاهد خصوصاً الكسوة فيقرر القاضي له نفقة غير أجرة الإرضاع وغير أجرة الحضانة . فعلى هذا تجب على الأب ثلاثة أجرة الرضاع وأجرة الحضانة ونفقة الولد. أما أجرة الرضاع فقد صرحوا بها هنا وأما أجرة الحضانة فصرح بها قارئ الهداية في فتاواه، وأما نفقة الولد فقد صرحوا بها في الإجارات في إجارة الظئر قال الزيلعي فيها: والطعام والثياب على الوالد، وما ذكره محمد في الدهن والريحان على الظئر فهو على عادة أهل الكوفة اهـ. فالحاصل أن الأم ليس عليها إلا الإرضاع وإصلاح طعامه وغسل ثيابه. لكن في الخانية وبعد الفطام يفرض القاضي نفقة الصغير على طاقة الأب ويدفع إلى الأم حتى تنفق على الأولاد اهـ . إلا أن يقال إن مراده النفقة الكاملة بخلافها في زمن الرضاع فإنها قليلة. وفي المجتبى : وإذا كان للصبي مال فمؤنة الرضاع ونفقته بعد الفطام في مال الصغير ومدة الرضاع ثلاثة أوقات : أدنى وهو حول ونصف، وأوسط وهو حولان ونصف حتى لو نقص عن الحولين لا يكون شططاً ولو زاد لا يكون تعدياً فلو استغنى الولد دون الحولين ففطمته في هذه لما قدمناه آنفاً عن البدائع أنها ترضع عند الأم فعلم أنه عند عدم استحقاقها لأجرة الرضاع لا ينزع الولد منها بخلاف ما لو لم تستحق أجرة الحضانة لوجود المتبرعة فإنه ينزع منها قوله : (والصحيح أنه يقال للام الخ قال الرملي : قيده في الخانية والبزازية والخلاصة والظهيرية وكثير من الكتب بكون الأب معسراً. فظاهره تخلف الحكم المذكور مع يساره فليحرر، وأنت خبير بأن المفهوم في التصانيف حجة يعمل به تأمل قوله : ولا تقاس على العمة الخ) جواب عما قد يقال إنها مثل العمة بجامع التبرع من كل فتلحق بها فأجاب بالفرق وهو أن العمة حاضنة في الجملة فلها استحقاق بخلاف الأجنبية. وأيضاً فإن العمة أشفق عليه من الأجنبية فلا تقاس عليها قوله : (وقد كثر السؤال عن المسألة) قال الرملي : وقد سئلت عن صغيرة لها أم وبنت ابن عم تطلب الأم زيادة عن أجر المثل وبنت ابن العم تريد حضانتها مجاناً فأجبت بأنها تدفع إلى الأم لكن بأجر المثل لا بالزيادة لأن بنت ابن العم كالأجنبية لا حق لها في الحضانة أصلاً فلا يعتبر تبرعها على ما ظهر لهذا الشارح وهو تفقه حسن صحيح في دفع الصغير للمتبرعة الأجنبية ضرراً به لقصور شفقتها عليه فلا يعتبر معه الضرر في المال لأن حرمته دون حرمته، ولذلك اختلف الحكم في نحو العمة والخالة مع الإعسار، فإذا كان موسراً لا يدفع إليهما كما يفيده تقييد أكثر الكتب إذ لا ضرر على الموسر في دفع الأجرة، وبه تتحرر هذه المسألة فافهم هذا التحرير واغتنمه فقد قل من تفطن له والله تعالى الموفق. بهذا وقد تقدم في الحضانة في شرح قوله : ثم العمات أنه لاحق لبنات الأعمام والأخوال لأنهن غير محرم قوله : فصرح بها قارئ الهداية في فتاواه حيث قال : سئل هل تستحق المطلقة أجرة حضانة ولدها خاصة من غير إرضاع له أم لا ؟ أجاب نعم تستحق أجرة على الحضانة، وكذا إن احتاج الصغير إلى خادم يلزم الأب به ويدل عليه أيضاً ما أن التقييد بإعسار الأب مر من يفيد أنه لو كان موسراً لا يدفع إلى العمة أي بل يؤمر الأب بدفع الأجرة للأم قوله : (وأوسط وهو بسبب لأن 1 هـ. اليسار
Another thing, as is observed, especially clothing: the judge assesses for him maintenance apart from the breastfeeding fee and apart from the custody fee. Accordingly, three [expenses] are obligatory on the father: the breastfeeding fee, the custody fee, and the child's maintenance. As for the breastfeeding fee, they have explicitly stated it here. As for the custody fee, Qari al-Hidayah explicitly stated it in his fatwas. As for the child's maintenance, they have explicitly stated it in the [chapters of] hire in the hiring of a wet nurse. Al-Zayla'i said therein: 'And food and clothing are upon the father; and what Muhammad mentioned about oil and perfume being upon the wet nurse is according to the custom of the people of Kufa.' End. So the summary is that the mother is responsible only for breastfeeding, preparing his food, and washing his clothes. But in al-Khaniyya: And after weaning, the judge assesses the child's maintenance according to the father's ability and gives it to the mother so that she spends on the children. End. Except that it may be said that he means full maintenance, unlike during the breastfeeding period, for it is small. And in al-Mujtaba: If the child has property, then the cost of breastfeeding and his maintenance after weaning are from the child's property. And the duration of breastfeeding has three times: the minimum is one and a half years, the middle is two and a half years, such that if it is less than two years it is not excessive, and if it exceeds it is not transgression. If the child becomes self-sufficient before two years and she weans him, then due to what we mentioned earlier from al-Bada'i: she breastfeeds him with the mother. So it is known that when she is not entitled to the breastfeeding fee, the child is not taken from her, unlike if she is not entitled to the custody fee due to the existence of a volunteer, then he is taken from her. His statement: (And the correct view is that the mother is told, etc.) Al-Ramli said: It is restricted in al-Khaniyya, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Khulasa, al-Zahiriya, and many books to the father being in financial difficulty. So its apparent meaning is that the mentioned ruling is different in case of his wealth, so let it be investigated. And you are aware that the understood meaning in the works is a proof that is acted upon, consider. His statement: (And it is not measured against the paternal aunt, etc.) [This is] a response to what might be said: she is like the paternal aunt due to the common factor of volunteering in everything, so she is annexed to her. So he answered with the difference: the paternal aunt is a custodian in general so she has a right, unlike the foreign woman. Also, the paternal aunt is more compassionate towards him than the foreign woman, so she is not measured against her. His statement: (And the question about this issue has become frequent) Al-Ramli said: I was asked about a young girl who has a mother and a paternal uncle's daughter; the mother demands more than the like wage, and the paternal uncle's daughter wants to have custody of her for free. So I answered that she is given to the mother, but for the like wage, not for the increase, because the paternal uncle's daughter is like a foreign woman; she has no right to custody at all, so her volunteering is not considered, according to what appears to this commentator. And it is good and correct jurisprudence in giving the child to a volunteering foreign woman is harmful to him due to the lack of her compassion for him, so harm in wealth is not considered alongside it because its sanctity is less than his sanctity. Therefore, the ruling differs concerning the paternal aunt and maternal aunt with regard to financial difficulty. If he is wealthy, he is not given to them, as is indicated by the restriction in most books, for there is no harm on the wealthy in paying the fee. With this, this issue is resolved, so understand this analysis and seize it, for few have grasped it, and Allah Almighty is the Giver of success. With this, and it has preceded in custody in the commentary on his statement: 'then the paternal aunts' that the daughters of paternal uncles and maternal uncles have no right because they are not mahrams. His statement: So Qari al-Hidayah explicitly stated it in his fatwas where he said: 'Was a divorced woman asked: Does she deserve a custody fee for her child specifically without breastfeeding him?' He answered: 'Yes, she deserves a fee for custody, and likewise if the child needs a servant, it is obligated on the father.' And it also indicates that the restriction to the father's financial difficulty that was mentioned implies that if he is wealthy, he is not given to the paternal aunt, rather the father is ordered to pay the fee to the mother. His statement: (and the middle is... because... 1 H. [the end]
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the father owes three separate categories of expenses for the child: (1) breastfeeding fee (ujrat al-rida'), (2) custody fee (ujrat al-hadana), and (3) general child maintenance (nafaqat al-walad) covering food, clothing, etc. The author synthesizes earlier sources: the breastfeeding fee is widely stated, the custody fee is affirmed by Qari al-Hidayah in his fatwa, and general maintenance is mentioned in sections on hiring a wet nurse. The mother's duties are limited to breastfeeding, preparing food, and washing clothes; all other expenses are on the father. If the child has property, expenses come from that property. The duration of breastfeeding is optimally two years but may be extended or shortened. The passage also revisits the earlier dispute: the restriction to the father's financial difficulty implies that if the father is wealthy, he cannot give the child to a paternal aunt offering free care; instead, he must pay the mother. The commentary stresses that a foreign woman has no right to custody and her offer is not considered because of insufficient compassion. The conclusion is that the custody fee is separate and obligatory; the father must pay it if he can, and the mother's right to custody cannot be overridden by a free offer from a non-relative.

Key Terms
أجرة الحضانة (ujrat al-hadana): Fee for the mother's custody of the child, distinct from breastfeeding fee. Obligatory on father according to later Hanafi fatwa.
نفقة الولد (nafaqat al-walad): General child maintenance including food, clothing, and other necessities beyond breastfeeding and custody.
مدة الرضاع (muddatal-rida'): Duration of breastfeeding: minimum 1.5 years, optimal 2.5 years; can be shorter if child is weaned early.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can give the child to a volunteer relative like a paternal aunt to avoid paying the mother.
B) He must pay the mother's custody fee even if a volunteer offers free care.
C) He is exempt from all fees because the child can be cared for by relatives.
D) The mother's right to fee is forfeited if she demands more than the norm.

Key Takeaway
A father owes three distinct wajibat: breastfeeding fee, custody fee, and general maintenance; wealth does not allow avoiding the mother's custody fee.

Custody Fee: When Father is Wealthy vs Insolvent
Resolving custody fee when father is wealthy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a wealthy father must pay the custody fee to the mother even if a relative offers free custody, and distinguish the cases of paternal aunt vs foreign woman.

Core Idea
A wealthy father cannot bypass the mother's custody fee by accepting free care from a non-custodian relative.

This lesson focuses on the second half of the passage, where the author resolves a common family law dilemma: can a father give his child to a relative offering free custody to avoid paying the mother? The answer hinges on the father's financial status and the nature of the volunteer. Understanding this nuance is critical for correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition: father's financial ability
The passage states that the earlier ruling (about giving child to volunteer) is restricted to the father being 'mu'sir' (insolvent). This implies that when he is 'muyassar' (wealthy), the ruling differs.
The key phrase is 'قيده في الخانية ... بكون الأب معسراً'. The restriction (taqyid) is a legal indicator.
2
Understand the implication of the restriction
The author says: 'فظاهره تخلف الحكم المذكور مع يساره' – the apparent meaning is that the mentioned ruling (giving to volunteer) is different when he is wealthy. So the mother cannot be bypassed.
This is a use of mafhum al-mukhalafa (inferential meaning from opposite case).
3
Analyze the analogy with the paternal aunt
The passage considers and rejects analogizing the foreign woman to the paternal aunt. The paternal aunt is a custodian (hadina) and has some right, so her volunteering might be acceptable when father is insolvent. But a foreign woman has no right, so her offer is never considered.
This shows that the reason (illa) is the lack of compassion and lack of right.
4
Apply the rule to the exemplified case
Al-Ramli's fatwa: a mother demands a higher fee; a paternal uncle's daughter offers free custody. The ruling: the child stays with the mother at the standard wage (ajr al-mithl), not the inflated fee, because the offer from the uncle's daughter is irrelevant.
The mother gets custody but only at standard pay; she cannot demand excess.

Three Obligations of Father for Child Maintenance
States three expenses father must pay for child: nursing fees, custody fees, and maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three financial obligations of the father toward his child and explain the scope of each based on the Hanafi sources cited.

Core Idea
The father must pay nursing fees, custody fees, and maintenance—the mother only nurses and prepares food.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the precise financial duties of a father toward his young child. It distinguishes three separate obligations—nursing fees (ujrat al-rida'), custody fees (ujrat al-hadhanah), and general maintenance (nafaqat al-walad)—and explains that the mother's role is limited. Understanding these obligations helps ensure the child's welfare and clarifies the father's responsibility in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three obligations
List the three expenses the father must pay: nursing fees, custody fees, and child maintenance. Note that each has a distinct basis in the sources.
2
Trace each obligation's source
Nursing fees are commonly stated, custody fees are affirmed by Qari' al-Hidayah, and maintenance is detailed in al-Zayla'i's commentary. Recognize that the author is expanding the base ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
3
Analyze the mother's duties
The passage states the mother is only required to nurse, prepare food, and wash clothes. She is not entitled to separate payment for these beyond the father's three obligations.
4
Consider the custom-based ruling
The mention of oil and perfume being on the wet nurse is based on Kufan custom, not a fixed rule. This highlights how custom (urf) can affect subsidiary details.
5
Understand post-weaning adjustment
After weaning, the judge determines full maintenance according to the father's capacity and pays it to the mother. This contrasts with the nursing period when maintenance is minimal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيء آخر كما هو المشاهد خصوصاً الكسوة فيقرر القاضي له نفقة غير أجرة الإرضاع وغير أجرة الحضانة . فعلى هذا تجب على الأب ثلاثة أجرة الرضاع وأجرة الحضانة ونفقة الولد. أما أجرة الرضاع فقد صرحوا بها هنا وأما أجرة الحضانة فصرح بها قارئ الهداية في فتاواه، وأما نفقة الولد فقد صرحوا بها في الإجارات في إجارة الظئر قال الزيلعي فيها: والطعام والثياب على الوالد، وما ذكره محمد في الدهن والريحان على الظئر فهو على عادة أهل الكوفة اهـ. فالحاصل أن الأم ليس عليها إلا الإرضاع وإصلاح طعامه وغسل ثيابه. لكن في الخانية وبعد الفطام يفرض القاضي نفقة الصغير على طاقة الأب ويدفع إلى الأم حتى تنفق على الأولاد اهـ . إلا أن يقال إن مراده النفقة الكاملة بخلافها في زمن الرضاع فإنها قليلة.
Another matter, as is observed especially clothing, so the judge determines for him maintenance other than nursing fees and custody fees. So upon this, three things are obligatory upon the father: nursing fees, custody fees, and child maintenance. As for nursing fees, they have explicitly stated them here; as for custody fees, Qari' al-Hidayah explicitly stated them in his fatwas; as for child maintenance, they have explicitly stated it in the section on hiring (ijarat) in the hiring of a wet nurse. Al-Zayla'i said therein: 'Food and clothing are upon the father, and what Muhammad mentioned regarding oil and perfume being upon the wet nurse is according to the custom of the people of Kufa.' So the conclusion is that the mother is only obliged to nurse, prepare his food, and wash his clothes. However, in al-Khaniyyah: 'After weaning, the judge determines the maintenance of the young child according to the father's capacity and pays it to the mother so that she spends on the children.' Unless it is said that he means full maintenance, as opposed to during the nursing period when it is little.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It establishes three financial obligations upon the father for his child: ujrat al-rida' (nursing fees), ujrat al-hadhanah (custody fees), and nafaqat al-walad (child maintenance). The author explains that while nursing fees are widely mentioned, custody fees are confirmed by Qari' al-Hidayah's fatwa. Maintenance includes food and clothing based on the custom of Kufa, with oil and perfume being the wet nurse's responsibility. The mother's duties are limited to nursing, preparing food, and washing clothes. After weaning, the judge assesses maintenance based on the father's means and pays it to the mother. The phrase 'except that it is said' indicates that the mother's duty during nursing is less, so the maintenance amount is lower.

Key Terms
أجرة الرضاع (ujrat al-rida'): Fees paid to the mother for nursing the child.
أجرة الحضانة (ujrat al-hadhanah): Fees paid to the mother for physical custody of the child.
نفقة الولد (nafaqat al-walad): General maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter for the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The father must provide nursing fees, custody fees, and child maintenance; the mother's duties are limited to nursing, food preparation, and washing clothes.

Duration of Nursing and Entitlement to Fees: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nursing duration and fees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three nursing periods identified by Hanafi scholars, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute over the duration for fee entitlement, and apply the majority view to determine when nursing fees are due.

Core Idea
Nursing fees are wajib only within two years; the mother cannot claim beyond that even if she nursed longer.

This passage from al-Mujtaba clarifies a practical family law issue: for how long is a divorced mother entitled to payment for breastfeeding? The Hanafi school has three possible durations for the nursing period, but the entitlement to fees is settled by the majority at two years. Understanding this distinction between permissible nursing and paid nursing is essential for calculating maintenance obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three durations
The text lists three durations for the nursing period: minimal (1.5 years), average (2.5 years), and a standard (2 years). Note that the entitlement to fees is specifically tied to the two-year period.
2
Locate the permissibility of nursing after two years
According to the majority of scholars (except Khalaf ibn Ayyub), it is permissible for the mother to nurse after two years if the child is not yet independent. This is a distinct issue from fee entitlement.
Khalaf ibn Ayyub's dissent is noted but not relied upon.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on fees
For a divorced woman (mubannah), Abu Hanifa held that she is entitled to fees up to 2.5 years, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) limited it to 2 years. The majority of later scholars (akthar al-mashayikh) adopted the 2-year limit for all cases.
The dispute does not affect the permissibility of nursing, only the financial entitlement.
4
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
For fatwa, the relied-upon view is two years. A mother who nurses beyond two years may do so without additional compensation unless a new contract is made.
The commentator also clarifies that fees are not automatically due without a contract, correcting a misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى المجتبى : وإذا كان للصبي مال فمؤنة الرضاع ونفقته بعد الفطام في مال الصغير ومدة الرضاع ثلاثة أوقات : أدنى وهو حول ونصف، وأوسط وهو حولان ونصف حتى لو نقص عن الحولين لا يكون شططاً ولو زاد لا يكون تعدياً فلو استغنى الولد دون الحولين ففطمته في حول ونصف حل بالإجماع ولا تأثم، ولو لم يستغن بحولين حل لها أن ترضعه بعدهما عند عامة المشايخ إلا عند خلف بن أيوب وأما الكلام في استحقاق الأجرة فمنهم من قال إنه على الخلاف حتى إن المبانة تستحق إلى الحولين ونصف عنده وعندهما إلى حولين فقط، وأكثر المشايخ على أن مدة الرضاع في حق الأجرة حولان عند الكل حتى لا تستحق بعد الحولين إجماعاً وتستحق في الحولين إجماعاً. وظاهر كلامهم أن وجوب أجرة الرضاع لا تتوقف على عقد إجارة مع الأم بل تستحقه بالإرضاع مطلقاً في المدة المذكورة، وقد قدمنا أنه ليس بفقه.
And in al-Mujtaba: If the young child has wealth, then the expenses of nursing and his maintenance after weaning are from the child's wealth. The nursing period consists of three times: the minimum is one and a half years, the average is two and a half years, such that if it falls short of two years it is not excessive, and if it exceeds it is not transgression. So if the child becomes independent before two years and she weans him at one and a half years, it is permissible by consensus and she does not sin. And if he does not become independent by two years, it is permissible for her to nurse him after that according to the majority of scholars, except for Khalaf ibn Ayyub. As for the discussion of entitlement to fees, some say it is subject to disagreement: the divorced woman (mubannah) is entitled up to two and a half years according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) only up to two years. The majority of scholars hold that the nursing period regarding fees is two years according to all, so she is not entitled after two years by consensus, and she is entitled within two years by consensus. The apparent meaning of their statements is that the obligation of nursing fees does not depend on a contract of hire with the mother; rather, she is entitled to it by merely nursing absolutely within the mentioned period. But we have previously stated that this is not correct fiqh.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the duration of the nursing period and its effect on entitlement to fees. Al-Mujtaba defines three temporal lengths: minimal 1.5 years, average 2.5 years. Weaning before 2 years is allowed if the child is independent; after 2 years, nursing is permissible per majority except Khalaf ibn Ayyub. Regarding fees, there is disagreement: Abu Hanifa says the mubannah (irrevocably divorced) mother is entitled to fees up to 2.5 years, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad limit it to 2 years. The majority settle on 2 years for all, so fees are due only within that period. The commentator then notes that some scholars claim fees are owed automatically without a contract, but he dismisses this as incorrect fiqh.

Key Terms
مدة الرضاع (muddat al-rada'): The legal duration of the nursing period affecting entitlement to fees.
استحقاق الأجرة (istihqaq al-ujrah): Entitlement to receive nursing fees for breastfeeding.
المبانة (al-mubannah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (ba'in).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, for how long is a mother entitled to nursing fees?
A) 1.5 years
B) 2 years
C) 2.5 years
D) 3 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority sets the nursing fee period at two years; beyond that, no fees are owed without a new contract.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
6 min
Maintenance of Parents and Grandparents in Hanafi Fiqh
Establishes obligation of child to support parents and grandparents, with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the obligation of a child to support parents and grandparents in Hanafi law, and identify the exception when the child is poor.

Core Idea
A solvent child must support poor parents; a poor child is exempt unless the parent is infirm.

In this passage, the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq lays out the obligation of maintenance (nafaqah) for one's parents and grandparents. Building on the Quranic command to accompany parents with goodness, the Hanafi school establishes that a child is required to support his ascendants only if the child is financially solvent and the ascendants are poor. However, there is a nuanced discussion when the child himself is poor—whether he must support infirm parents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is providing maintenance to parents and grandparents. The ruling is wajib, but only under specific conditions.
This is not an absolute obligation; it depends on solvency and need.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 31:15: 'And accompany them with goodness.' The implication is that letting parents starve contradicts goodness.
The dalil is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala; the Hanafi school uses it to derive wujub.
3
Analyse the conditions
The child must be solvent (maysar) and the parent must be poor (faqir). This differs from wife's maintenance, which is due even if she is wealthy due to confinement.
If the parent has wealth, their own wealth is used first.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi nuance
Sources like al-Hidayah and al-Jawhara state that a poor son is generally not obligated, but if the parent is infirm (zamin) and cannot earn, the poor son must share maintenance.
The mother is treated like an infirm father.
5
Summarise the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: a solvent child must support poor parents; a poor child is exempt except when the parent is infirm.
This balances the child's incapacity with the parent's dire need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولأبويه وأجداده وجداته لو فقراء أي تجب النفقة لهؤلاء، أما الأبوان فلقوله تعالى وصاحبهما في الدنيا معروفاً [لقمان: ١٥] أنزلت في الأبوين الكافرين، وليس من المعروف أن الابن يعيش في نعم الله تعالى ويتركهما يموتان جوعاً. وأما الأجداد والجدات فلأنهما من الآباء والأمهات ولهذا يقوم الجد مقام الأب عند عدمه ولأنهم تسببوا لإحيائه فاستوجبوا عليه الإحياء بمنزلة الأبوين وشرط الفقر لأنه لو كان ذا مال فإيجاب النفقة ماله أولى من إيجابها في مال غيره بخلاف نفقة الزوجة حيث تجب مع الغنى لأنها تجب لأجل الحبس الدائم كرزق القاضي، ولو ادعى الولد غنى الأب وأنكره الأب فالقول للأب والبينة. قوله : (أو بهما فقر فقط) أي بدون زمانة، ولعل المراد بذلك أن لا يقدرا على العمل كما يأتي في عبارة الخانية وإلا فالكلام في المعسرين فما معنى استثناء ما إذا كان بهما فقر تأمل. قوله : ولا يجب على الابن الفقير نفقة والده الفقير الخ يوافق هذا قوله في فتح القدير وعلى الرجل أي الموسر حيث فسره بالموسر للاحتراز عن الفقير وكذا قال في متن الدرر وعلى الموسر يسار الفطرة لأصوله الفقراء الخ. ومثله في متن الملتقى والنقاية والمواهب وغيرها فكلهم قيدوا باليسار. وفي الاختيار وكافي الحاكم: ولا تجب النفقة على فقير إلا للزوجة وللولد الصغير ا.هـ. ومثله في الهداية ومقتضاه عدم وجوبها على الابن الفقير لأبيه. وفي الجوهرة: وإن كان الابن فقيراً والأب فقيراً صحيح البدن لم يجبر الابن على نفقته إلا أن يكون الأب زمناً لا يقدر على الكسب فيشارك الابن في نفقته والأم الفقيرة كالأب الزمن. وفي كافي الحاكم: ويجبر الرجل الموسر على نفقة أبيه وأمه إذا كانا محتاجين قلت: لكن يخالف هذا ما سيأتي
His statement: 'And for his parents and his grandparents and grandmothers if they are poor.' That is, maintenance is obligatory for these. As for the parents, due to His saying 'And accompany them in this world with goodness' [Luqman 31:15], revealed about disbelieving parents. It is not from goodness that the son lives in Allah's blessings and leaves them to die of hunger. As for grandparents and grandmothers, because they are from the fathers and mothers, and for this reason the grandfather takes the place of the father in his absence, and because they were the cause of his (the child's) existence, so they deserve from him the continuation of existence, like the parents. The condition of poverty is necessary because if he (the parent) had wealth, imposing maintenance on his own wealth is more appropriate than imposing it on the wealth of others, unlike the wife's maintenance which is obligatory even with wealth because it is for permanent confinement like the salary of a judge. If the child claims the father's wealth and the father denies it, the father's word is taken with his oath. His statement: 'or if both are simply poor' i.e., without infirmity. Perhaps what is meant by that is that they are unable to work, as will come in the expression of al-Khaniyyah; otherwise, the discussion is about the insolvent, so what is the meaning of excepting the case where both are poor? Reflect. His statement: 'And it is not obligatory upon the poor son to support his poor father, etc.' This agrees with his statement in Fath al-Qadir: 'And upon the man' meaning the solvent, because he interpreted it as the solvent to exclude the poor. Similarly, it is stated in the text of al-Durar: 'And upon the solvent with the ability of fitrah for his poor ancestors, etc.' And similar is in the texts of al-Multaqa, al-Niqaya, al-Mawahib, and others; all restricted it with solvency. In al-Ikhtiyar and Kafi al-Hakim: 'Maintenance is not obligatory upon a poor person except for the wife and the young child.' Similarly in al-Hidayah, which implies non-obligation upon a poor son for his father. In al-Jawhara: 'If the son is poor and the father is poor and physically sound, the son is not compelled to support him unless the father is infirm and unable to earn, then the son shares in his maintenance, and the poor mother is like the infirm father.' In Kafi al-Hakim: 'A solvent man is compelled to support his father and mother if they are needy.' I say: But this contradicts what will come later.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligation of a child to support his parents and grandparents. The proof is from Quran 31:15, which commands goodness to parents even if they are disbelievers; letting them starve contradicts goodness. Grandparents are included because they are like parents. The condition of poverty is essential because if they have wealth, their own wealth should be used first. This contrasts with wife's maintenance, which is due even if she is wealthy because of marital confinement. The passage then discusses a dispute: if the son is also poor, is he still liable? The relied-upon view is that the son must be solvent; a poor son is not obligated except to support his wife and young child. However, if the father is infirm (zamin), the poor son must share maintenance. The same applies to a poor mother. The commentator notes that various sources restrict the obligation to a solvent son, and a poor son is exempt except for extraordinary cases.

Key Terms
نفقة الأصول (nafaqat al-usul): Maintenance of ascendants (parents, grandparents).
إعسار (i'sar): Financial insolvency; a state that exempts a son from supporting parents except in special cases.
زمانة (zamanah): Chronic infirmity or disability preventing earning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is maintenance of a father obligatory upon his son?
A) Always, regardless of the son's wealth
B) Only if the son is solvent and the father is poor
C) Only if the father is infirm
D) Only if the father is a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Maintenance of parents is wajib on a solvent child for poor parents; a poor child is exempt unless the parent is infirm.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner

Obligation of Child to Support Poor Parents: The Wealth Condition
Establishing the wealth condition for parental maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a child must possess wealth equal to the nisab of zakat to be obligated to support poor parents and identify the Quranic proof for this obligation.

Core Idea
A child must be wealthy (possessing nisab of zakat) to be obligated to support poor parents.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a crucial condition in Hanafi fiqh: the obligation of a child to support his poor parents depends on the child's own wealth. While the Quran commands kindness to parents, the Hanafi school limits financial maintenance to those who can afford it without harming themselves or their dependents. The key term is 'yasar' (wealth sufficiency), defined as owning surplus wealth equal to the zakat nisab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is supporting poor parents. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) but only if the child meets the condition of wealth. Sate the general principle from the text.
2
Locate the condition (yasar)
The text repeatedly conditions the obligation on the child being 'wealthy' (musir). Find the definition of wealth: possessing nisab of zakat after meeting one's own and dependents' needs.
Check the definitions from al-Khaniyyah and al-Mujtaba.
3
Analyze the proof (Quranic verse)
The text refers to Surah Luqman 31:15. Understand how the command 'accompany them with goodness' (maruf) implies financial support when parents are in need, as it falls under ma'ruf.
The verse was revealed regarding pagan parents, so it applies even more to Muslim parents.
4
Confirm the zahir al-riwayah ruling
The author states that the position in the standard texts (like Kafi al-Hakim, al-Hidayah) is the zahir al-riwayah (transmitted majority view). Confirm that this is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
5
Note the exclusion of the poor child
The text explicitly states that a poor child is not obligated to support a poor parent who is able to work. Understand the logic: one's own need takes precedence (hadith 'begin with yourself').
Exception: if parent is disabled, see next lesson.

وبوجود قاض ثمة يأثم بسرقة ماله، وبإعطاء الابن مالاً يكفيه يجوز له أن يأخذ إلى أن تقع الكفاية، وبسرقته ما فوق الكفاية يأثم، وكذا إذا لم يكن محتاجاً ولم تكن نفقته عليه لا يجوز له أن يسرق مال ابنه اهـ. يفرض لهما نفقة على حدة .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ولا يجب على الابن الفقير نفقة والده الفقير حكماً إذا كان الوالد يقدر على العمل، وإن كان الوالد لا يقدر على عمل أو كان زمناً وللابن عيال كان على الابن أن يضم الأب إلى عياله وينفق على الكل والموسر في هذا الباب من يملك مالاً فاضلاً. عن نفقة عياله ويبلغ الفاضل مقداراً تجب فيه الزكاة اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : المختار في الفقير الكسوب أن يدخل الأبوين في النفقة. وقيد كسبه قال في الذخيرة وقال بعض العلماء: يجبر الابن على أن يدخل الأب في قوته إذا كان ما يصيب الابن من ذلك القوت يقيم بدنه ولا يضره إضراراً يمنعه من الكسب. وروي عن أبي يوسف أيضاً لأنه لو لم يفعل ضاع الأب إلا أن في ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا لا يجبر على ذلك لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ابدأ بنفسك ثم بمن تحول هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا كان الابن وحده فلو له زوجة وأولاد صغار وباقي المسألة بحالها، فالقاضي يجبره على أن الواحد في طعام الواحد يتفاحش الضرر. ثم قال : هذا كله إذا كان الأب عاجزاً عن الكسب قوله : كان على الابن أن يضم الأب إلى عياله الخ) ظاهره أنه يطعمه مع عياله وكثيراً ما يسئل عنه وهو الأم تريد أن تأخذ من ابنها النفقة تنفق هي على نفسها لأنها إذا كانت في بيته تؤذيها زوجته وتشتمها فهل تجاب إلى ذلك؟ ظاهره لا لكن هذا إذا كان الابن فقيراً، أما الموسر فالظاهر أنه يلزمه الدفع إلى أبيه أو أمه لأن ذلك حقهما فلهما قبضه منه وسيذكر المؤلف ما يؤيده قبيل قوله وصح بيع عرض ابنه» قوله : ( وقيد بفقرهم فقط) أي ولم يقيد بكونهم عاجزين عن الكسب قوله: (قيل هو ظاهر الضرر أن
His statement: 'Or with poverty only' meaning without disability, and perhaps what is meant is that they are unable to work, as will come in the expression of al-Khaniyyah; otherwise the discussion is about those in difficulty, so what is the meaning of excepting when there is poverty in them? Reflect. His statement: 'And it is not obligatory upon a poor son to spend on his poor father, etc.' This agrees with his statement in Fath al-Qadir: 'And upon the man, meaning the wealthy one' where he interpreted it as wealthy to exclude the poor. Similarly said in the text of al-Durar: 'And upon the wealthy with the capacity of zakat for his poor parents, etc.' And similar in the text of al-Multaqa, al-Nuqaya, al-Mawahib, and others; all qualified with wealth (yasar). In al-Ikhtiyar and Kafi al-Hakim: 'Maintenance is not obligatory upon a poor person except for the wife and the young child.' End quote. Similarly in al-Hidayah, and its implication is the non-obligation upon a poor son for his father. In al-Jawharah: 'If the son is poor and the father is poor and sound of body, the son is not compelled to spend on him unless the father is disabled, unable to earn, in which case he shares in his maintenance, and the poor mother is like the disabled father.' In Kafi al-Hakim: 'A wealthy man is compelled to spend on his father and mother if they are needy.' I say: 'But this contradicts what will come later for the son.' In al-Mubtagha (with a dotted letter): 'If the father is in need and the son refuses to spend on him, and there is no judge to whom he can refer the matter, he may steal from his son's wealth. If there is a judge present, he sins by stealing his wealth. If the son gives him enough wealth, he may take up to sufficiency; stealing above sufficiency is sinful. Likewise if he is not in need and maintenance is not obligatory upon the son, he may not steal from his son's wealth.' End quote. It is absolute regarding the son and not restricted by wealth, although it is restricted by it, according to what is in Sharh al-Tahawi: 'A son is not compelled to spend on his destitute parents if he is destitute, unless they are disabled or only poor, in which case they enter with the son and eat with him, and separate maintenance is not prescribed for them.' End quote. In al-Khaniyyah: 'It is not obligatory upon a poor son to spend on his poor father as a legal ruling if the father is able to work. But if the father is unable to work or is disabled, and the son has dependents, then the son must include the father among his dependents and spend on all. The wealthy in this chapter is one who possesses surplus wealth beyond the maintenance of his dependents, and the surplus reaches an amount on which zakat is obligatory.' End quote. In al-Khulasah: 'The chosen position regarding a poor breadwinner is that he includes the parents in maintenance.' It is restricted to their poverty only, because if he is poor and able to earn, then the son is compelled to spend on him; this is the saying of al-Sarakhsi. al-Halwani said: 'He is not compelled.' Near from al-Fath: 'If both, i.e., father and son, are breadwinners, the son must earn and spend on the father.' End quote. In al-Mujtaba: 'In the book, the condition for spending on parents is that the son be wealthy and possess the nisab of zakat. al-Khassaf considered the ability to spend and did not consider wealth. Then he reported two sayings concerning the issue of al-Fath. So it is known that what the author mentioned is the apparent of the narration (zahir al-riwayah) because it agrees with what is in Kafi al-Hakim and the standard texts. As for considering ability to earn, it is the narration of al-Khassaf, and upon it al-Bada'i proceeded.' His statement: 'And the son has dependents' is restricted to that because if he had no dependents, he would not include the father with himself since his earning would not suffice both. He said in al-Dhakhirah: 'Some scholars said: The son is compelled to include the father in his food if what the son gets from that food sustains his body and does not harm him with harm that prevents him from earning.' It is also reported from Abu Yusuf, because if he does not do so, the father would be lost. However, in the apparent of the narration (zahir al-riwayah) from our companions, he is not compelled to do so due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: 'Begin with yourself, then with those you support.' This is what we mentioned when the son is alone. But if he has a wife and young children, and the rest of the issue remains as it is, the judge compels him to include the father in his earnings and make him like one of his dependents, but does not compel him to give him something separately. The difference is that if he includes him in the food of his dependents, it is less, because the food of four when divided among five does not harm each one excessively; whereas if one is included in the food of one, the harm becomes excessive. Then he said: 'All this is when the father is unable to earn.' His statement: 'The son must include the father with his dependents' appears that he feeds him with his dependents. One is often asked about it: the mother wants to take maintenance from her son to spend on herself because when she is in his house, his wife harms and insults her. Is her request granted? Apparently not, but this is when the son is poor. As for the wealthy, apparently he is obliged to pay to his father or mother because that is their right, so they may take it from him. The author will mention what supports this just before his statement: 'And the sale of his son's commodity is valid.' His statement: 'And restricted to their poverty only' meaning he did not restrict them to being unable to earn. His statement: 'It is said that it is apparent harm that' (cut off).
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the obligation of a son (or child) to support his parents when they are poor. It is a classic Hanafi exploration with multiple intra-madhhab positions. The core ruling is that a child must support poor parents, with evidence from the Quran (Surah Luqman 15) and rational necessity. However, the key condition is that the child must be wealthy (musir) — possessing surplus wealth equal to the nisab of zakat after his own needs and those of his dependents. If the child is also poor, the obligation is generally not imposed unless the parent is disabled (zamin) and unable to earn. The passage surveys multiple authorities: al-Ikhtiyar, Kafi al-Hakim, al-Hidayah, al-Jawharah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Khulasah, al-Mujtaba, among others. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that the son must be wealthy; the narration of al-Khassaf considers ability to pay rather than wealth, but this is not the preferred view. There is also a discussion of what happens if the son has dependents: if the son is alone, he is not compelled to share his food with a parent who can work; but if the son has a wife and children, he is compelled to include the parent as a dependent (yudkhiluhu fi 'iyalihi) rather than pay separately. This is because the harm of dividing food among many is less than sharing one-to-one. A related issue: if the parent is unable to earn (disabled), the son must include him in his household and feed him with his family. The passage also addresses an extreme remedy: if no judge is available and the father is needy and the son refuses, the father may take his son's wealth by stealth up to sufficiency, but sins if he takes more or if a judge is present. For the mother, if she wants separate maintenance to avoid conflict with her daughter-in-law, the answer is that if the son is poor, she is not entitled to separate maintenance; but if he is wealthy, he must pay. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual evidence, customary practice, and harm prevention.

Key Terms
يسار (yasar): Wealth sufficiency; in this context, possessing surplus wealth beyond one's own and dependents' needs, equivalent to the nisab of zakat.
زمانة (zamanah): Chronic disability or infirmity preventing the parent from earning a living.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from the six core books of Imam Muhammad; here, it is the majority view that wealth is a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah position in this lesson, what is the condition for a son to be obligated to support his poor parents?
A) The son must have any surplus income
B) The son must possess wealth equal to the nisab of zakat
C) The son must be able to work
D) The parents must be disabled

Key Takeaway
A child's obligation to support poor parents is conditional on the child's wealth (possession of zakat nisab); a poor child is not compelled unless the parent is disabled.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Intra-Hanafi Positions and Special Cases for Parental Maintenance
Intra-Hanafi dispute and special cases for parental inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the intra-Hanafi positions of al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani regarding a poor breadwinning son, and apply the ruling that a son with dependents must include a disabled parent in his household without separate maintenance.

Core Idea
A poor son must include a disabled parent in his household but is not compelled to support a parent who can work.

This second part of the passage delves deeper into the nuances of parental maintenance. It presents a clear intra-Hanafi disagreement between al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani regarding a poor son who is able to earn (kasub). It also clarifies a practical scenario: when the son has dependents (wife and children), the judge compels him to include a disabled parent in his household as one of the dependents, rather than paying a separate stipend. This prevents excessive harm to the son's family.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute regarding the poor breadwinning son
The text presents two views: al-Sarakhsi says a poor son who can earn must be compelled to support his parents; al-Halwani says he is not compelled. Note which view is considered the 'chosen' (mukhtar) in al-Khulasah.
Al-Sarakhsi's view is mentioned as an exception to the general rule.
2
Analyze the scenario of the son with dependents
When the son has a wife and children, the judge compels him to include a disabled father in his household (yudkhiluhu fi 'iyalihi). Understand the reasoning: dividing food among many causes less harm than when the son is alone.
This is based on the hadith 'begin with yourself' and the principle of harm prevention.
3
Understand the difference between including and separate maintenance
The son is not compelled to give a separate stipend to the parent; rather, he must include the parent in his own household's food. This is to minimize hardship.
If the son is alone, he is not compelled even to include the parent.
4
Apply the ruling to the mother seeking separate maintenance
If the mother wants separate maintenance to avoid conflict with her daughter-in-law, the answer depends on the son's wealth. If the son is poor, she is not entitled. If wealthy, he must pay.
This is a common contemporary question.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi for special cases
The relied-upon position is that a poor son with dependents must include a disabled parent in his household. A poor son without dependents is not compelled. A wealthy son must support separately.

His statement: 'Or with poverty only' meaning without disability, and perhaps what is meant is that they are unable to work, as will come in the expression of al-Khaniyyah; otherwise the discussion is about those in difficulty, so what is the meaning of excepting when there is poverty in them? Reflect. His statement: 'And it is not obligatory upon a poor son to spend on his poor father, etc.' This agrees with his statement in Fath al-Qadir: 'And upon the man, meaning the wealthy one' where he interpreted it as wealthy to exclude the poor. Similarly said in the text of al-Durar: 'And upon the wealthy with the capacity of zakat for his poor parents, etc.' And similar in the text of al-Multaqa, al-Nuqaya, al-Mawahib, and others; all qualified with wealth (yasar). In al-Ikhtiyar and Kafi al-Hakim: 'Maintenance is not obligatory upon a poor person except for the wife and the young child.' End quote. Similarly in al-Hidayah, and its implication is the non-obligation upon a poor son for his father. In al-Jawharah: 'If the son is poor and the father is poor and sound of body, the son is not compelled to spend on him unless the father is disabled, unable to earn, in which case he shares in his maintenance, and the poor mother is like the disabled father.' In Kafi al-Hakim: 'A wealthy man is compelled to spend on his father and mother if they are needy.' I say: 'But this contradicts what will come later for the son.' In al-Mubtagha (with a dotted letter): 'If the father is in need and the son refuses to spend on him, and there is no judge to whom he can refer the matter, he may steal from his son's wealth. If there is a judge present, he sins by stealing his wealth. If the son gives him enough wealth, he may take up to sufficiency; stealing above sufficiency is sinful. Likewise if he is not in need and maintenance is not obligatory upon the son, he may not steal from his son's wealth.' End quote. It is absolute regarding the son and not restricted by wealth, although it is restricted by it, according to what is in Sharh al-Tahawi: 'A son is not compelled to spend on his destitute parents if he is destitute, unless they are disabled or only poor, in which case they enter with the son and eat with him, and separate maintenance is not prescribed for them.' End quote. In al-Khaniyyah: 'It is not obligatory upon a poor son to spend on his poor father as a legal ruling if the father is able to work. But if the father is unable to work or is disabled, and the son has dependents, then the son must include the father among his dependents and spend on all. The wealthy in this chapter is one who possesses surplus wealth beyond the maintenance of his dependents, and the surplus reaches an amount on which zakat is obligatory.' End quote. In al-Khulasah: 'The chosen position regarding a poor breadwinner is that he includes the parents in maintenance.' It is restricted to their poverty only, because if he is poor and able to earn, then the son is compelled to spend on him; this is the saying of al-Sarakhsi. al-Halwani said: 'He is not compelled.' Near from al-Fath: 'If both, i.e., father and son, are breadwinners, the son must earn and spend on the father.' End quote. In al-Mujtaba: 'In the book, the condition for spending on parents is that the son be wealthy and possess the nisab of zakat. al-Khassaf considered the ability to spend and did not consider wealth. Then he reported two sayings concerning the issue of al-Fath. So it is known that what the author mentioned is the apparent of the narration (zahir al-riwayah) because it agrees with what is in Kafi al-Hakim and the standard texts. As for considering ability to earn, it is the narration of al-Khassaf, and upon it al-Bada'i proceeded.' His statement: 'And the son has dependents' is restricted to that because if he had no dependents, he would not include the father with himself since his earning would not suffice both. He said in al-Dhakhirah: 'Some scholars said: The son is compelled to include the father in his food if what the son gets from that food sustains his body and does not harm him with harm that prevents him from earning.' It is also reported from Abu Yusuf, because if he does not do so, the father would be lost. However, in the apparent of the narration (zahir al-riwayah) from our companions, he is not compelled to do so due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: 'Begin with yourself, then with those you support.' This is what we mentioned when the son is alone. But if he has a wife and young children, and the rest of the issue remains as it is, the judge compels him to include the father in his earnings and make him like one of his dependents, but does not compel him to give him something separately. The difference is that if he includes him in the food of his dependents, it is less, because the food of four when divided among five does not harm each one excessively; whereas if one is included in the food of one, the harm becomes excessive. Then he said: 'All this is when the father is unable to earn.' His statement: 'The son must include the father with his dependents' appears that he feeds him with his dependents. One is often asked about it: the mother wants to take maintenance from her son to spend on herself because when she is in his house, his wife harms and insults her. Is her request granted? Apparently not, but this is when the son is poor. As for the wealthy, apparently he is obliged to pay to his father or mother because that is their right, so they may take it from him. The author will mention what supports this just before his statement: 'And the sale of his son's commodity is valid.' His statement: 'And restricted to their poverty only' meaning he did not restrict them to being unable to earn. His statement: 'It is said that it is apparent harm that' (cut off).
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the obligation of a son (or child) to support his parents when they are poor. It is a classic Hanafi exploration with multiple intra-madhhab positions. The core ruling is that a child must support poor parents, with evidence from the Quran (Surah Luqman 15) and rational necessity. However, the key condition is that the child must be wealthy (musir) — possessing surplus wealth equal to the nisab of zakat after his own needs and those of his dependents. If the child is also poor, the obligation is generally not imposed unless the parent is disabled (zamin) and unable to earn. The passage surveys multiple authorities: al-Ikhtiyar, Kafi al-Hakim, al-Hidayah, al-Jawharah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Khulasah, al-Mujtaba, among others. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that the son must be wealthy; the narration of al-Khassaf considers ability to pay rather than wealth, but this is not the preferred view. There is also a discussion of what happens if the son has dependents: if the son is alone, he is not compelled to share his food with a parent who can work; but if the son has a wife and children, he is compelled to include the parent as a dependent (yudkhiluhu fi 'iyalihi) rather than pay separately. This is because the harm of dividing food among many is less than sharing one-to-one. A related issue: if the parent is unable to earn (disabled), the son must include him in his household and feed him with his family. The passage also addresses an extreme remedy: if no judge is available and the father is needy and the son refuses, the father may take his son's wealth by stealth up to sufficiency, but sins if he takes more or if a judge is present. For the mother, if she wants separate maintenance to avoid conflict with her daughter-in-law, the answer is that if the son is poor, she is not entitled to separate maintenance; but if he is wealthy, he must pay. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual evidence, customary practice, and harm prevention.

Key Terms
يسار (yasar): Wealth sufficiency; in this context, possessing surplus wealth beyond one's own and dependents' needs, equivalent to the nisab of zakat.
زمانة (zamanah): Chronic disability or infirmity preventing the parent from earning a living.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from the six core books of Imam Muhammad; here, it is the majority view that wealth is a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A poor son with dependents must include a disabled parent in his household, but is not compelled to give separate maintenance; a poor son without dependents is not compelled at all.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
