Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Child's Obligation to Support Parents: Wealth vs. Earning Ability
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions for child's maintenance of parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a child's obligation to support parents and distinguish between the positions of al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani regarding the parent's ability to earn.

Core Idea
A child must support a poor parent only if the child is wealthy (zakat-able surplus), but scholars differ on whether a parent's ability to work removes the obligation.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author examines a key question in Hanafi nafaqah: when is a child obliged to support a needy parent? The text presents multiple rulings from earlier Hanafi authorities and highlights an internal disagreement between al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani. We will unpack the conditions and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the key condition
The act is the child's obligation to provide nafaqah for parents. The key condition stated in the matn is that the child must be wealthy (musir).
Wealth is defined specifically in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Define 'wealthy' (musir) in this context
According to the text, musir means having surplus beyond dependents' needs equal to the zakat nisab.
This definition ties nafaqah obligations to zakat liability.
3
Examine the exception for disabled parents
Even if the child is not wealthy, if the parent is disabled (zamanah) or extremely poor, the child must include them in the household.
This exception is from Sharh al-Tahawi.
4
Analyze the dispute: al-Sarakhsi vs. al-Halwani
Al-Sarakhsi holds that if the parent is able to work, the obligation remains if the parent is poor. Al-Halwani says the obligation is negated if the parent can earn.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the zahir al-riwayah position
The author concludes that the matn's condition (child's wealth) is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The alternative view (considering earning ability) is a narration from al-Khassaf.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah over nawadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لللابن. وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة : إذا كان الأب محتاجاً وأبى الابن أن ينفق عليه وليس ثمة قاض يرفع الأمر إليه له أن يسرق من مال ابنه وبوجود قاض ثمة يأثم بسرقة ماله، وبإعطاء الابن مالاً يكفيه يجوز له أن يأخذ إلى أن تقع الكفاية، وبسرقته ما فوق الكفاية يأثم، وكذا إذا لم يكن محتاجاً ولم تكن نفقته عليه لا يجوز له أن يسرق مال ابنه اهـ. وأطلق في الابن ولم يقيده بالغنا مع أنه مقيد به لما في شرح الطحاوي ولا يجبر الابن على نفقة أبويه المعسرين إذا كان معسراً إلا إذا كان بهما زمانة أو بهما فقر فقط فإنهما يدخلان مع الابن ويأكلان معه ولا يفرض لهما نفقة على حدة .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ولا يجب على الابن الفقير نفقة والده الفقير حكماً إذا كان الوالد يقدر على العمل، وإن كان الوالد لا يقدر على عمل أو كان زمناً وللابن عيال كان على الابن أن يضم الأب إلى عياله وينفق على الكل والموسر في هذا الباب من يملك مالاً فاضلاً. عن نفقة عياله ويبلغ الفاضل مقداراً تجب فيه الزكاة اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : المختار في الفقير الكسوب أن يدخل الأبوين في النفقة. وقيد بفقرهم فقط لأنه لو كان فقيراً وله قدرة على الكسب فإن الابن يجبر على نفقته وهو قول السرخسي. وقال الحلواني : لا يجبر قريباً عن الفتح لو كان كل منهما أي الأب والابن كسوباً يجب أن يكتسب الابن وينفق على الأب ا هـ. وفي المجتبى : شرط في الكتاب لنفقة الوالدين كون الابن موسراً ويملك نصاب الزكاة، واعتبر الخصاف القدرة على الإنفاق ولم يعتبر اليسار ثم حكى في مسألة الفتح قولين. فعلم أن ما ذكره المؤلف هو ظاهر الرواية لموافقته لما في كافي الحاكم والمتون، وأما اعتبار القدرة على الكسب فهو رواية الخصاف وعليها مشى في البدائع
For the son. In al-Mubtagha: if the father is needy and the son refuses to support him and there is no judge to refer the matter to, he may steal from his son's wealth. If there is a judge, he sins by stealing his wealth. If the son gives him enough, he may take until sufficiency is reached. If he steals above sufficiency, he sins. Similarly, if he is not needy and maintenance is not obligatory on him, he may not steal his son's wealth. He (the author) used the word 'son' generally without qualifying it by wealth, but it is qualified by what is in Sharh al-Tahawi: the son is not forced to support his poor parents if he himself is poor, unless they are disabled or merely poor, then they enter with the son and eat with him, and no separate maintenance is prescribed for them. In al-Khaniyya: maintenance is not obligatory on the poor son for his poor father in legal ruling if the father is able to work. If the father is unable to work or is disabled and the son has dependents, the son must include the father among his dependents and provide for all. The wealthy in this context is one who owns surplus wealth beyond the maintenance of his dependents, and the surplus reaches the amount on which zakat is obligatory. In al-Khulasa: the chosen view regarding the poor earner is that both parents are included in maintenance. He restricted it to their poverty only because if he is poor but able to earn, the son is forced to support him – this is the view of al-Sarakhsi. Al-Halwani said: he is not forced. Nearly from al-Fath: if both, i.e. the father and son, are earners, the son must earn and support the father. In al-Mujtaba: the condition in the book for maintenance of parents is that the son be wealthy, owning the nisab of zakat. Al-Khassaf considered ability to spend and did not consider wealth. Then he narrated two views on the issue of al-Fath. So it is known that what the author mentioned is the apparent narration, agreeing with what is in Kafi al-Hakim and the texts. As for considering ability to earn, it is the narration of al-Khassaf, and al-Bada'i relied on it.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and expansion of rules regarding child's obligation to support parents. It begins with a ruling from al-Mubtagha that if a father is needy and the son refuses to support, and there is no judge, the father may take from his son's wealth by theft if necessary, but only up to the amount of sufficiency. If a judge is available, theft is sinful. The commentary stresses that this is specific to need. Next, from Sharh al-Tahawi, a general principle is given: a poor son is not forced to support his poor parents unless the parents are disabled or extremely poor, in which case they are included in the son's household (eat with him). Then al-Khaniyya adds that if the father can work, no maintenance is due from a poor son; if the father cannot work and the son has dependents, the son must include the father. The definition of 'wealthy' (musir) here is having surplus beyond dependents' needs equal to zakat nisab. Then a dispute between al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani is presented: al-Sarakhsi holds that a poor but able-bodied father is entitled to maintenance from his son; al-Halwani disagrees. The comment from al-Fath says if both are earners, the son must earn and support the father. The author (of al-Bahr) notes that the explicit condition in al-Kanz (the matn) is the son's wealth, but al-Khassaf considered ability to spend. The author asserts that the matn's view (son must be wealthy) is the zahir al-riwaya, while al-Khassaf's view (consider ability to earn) is another narration followed in al-Bada'i.

Key Terms
الموسر (al-musir): One who owns surplus wealth beyond the maintenance of his dependents, and the surplus reaches the amount on which zakat is obligatory.
الكسوب (al-kasub): A person who is able to earn a living through work.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted ruling from the six works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah in the Hanafi school, what condition is required for a son to be obliged to support his poor father?
A) The son must be wealthy with surplus equal to zakat nisab.
B) The son must be able to earn, regardless of his wealth.
C) The father must be disabled and unable to work.
D) The son must have no dependents of his own.

Key Takeaway
The child's obligation to support parents in the Hanafi school is conditional on the child's wealth (zakat nisab surplus), but a dispute exists regarding the parent's earning ability, with the authoritative view relying on the child's wealth status.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Son with Dependents: Including the Father
Details the qualification for damm al-ab and its condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a son must include his father in his household and distinguish the Hanafi ruling from Abu Yusuf's narration.

Core Idea
A son with dependents must include his father in his household, but without separate allocation, only if it avoids excessive harm.

This lesson explores the qualification 'and the son has dependents' in the matn. The Hanafi school carefully balances the obligations toward parents and the son's own dependents, using the prophetic principle 'Begin with yourself' and the concept of excessive harm (tafawut fahish).

Guided Path
1
Identify the qualification
The matn says 'and the son has dependents'. Why is this qualification important? Without dependents, the son is not forced to include the father because his earnings would not suffice both.
The qualification prevents hardship on the son when alone.
2
Understand the dispute with Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf's narration forces the son even if alone, as long as the father would not be lost. But the zahir al-riwaya (apparent narration) does not force him, based on the hadith 'Begin with yourself'.
The zahir al-riwaya is the relied-upon position.
3
Apply the hadith 'Begin with yourself'
The hadith establishes priority: the son's own self and his dependents come first. Only when he has dependents does the father become included without causing excessive harm.
This is a key dalil for the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the difference when son has dependents
When the son has dependents, including the father in their food divides the food among more people, but the harm to each is not excessive. In contrast, adding one to a single person's food causes excessive harm.
This is a qiyas reasoning based on preventing harm.
5
Note the condition of father's inability to earn
The inclusion is only when the father is unable to earn (cajz). If the father can earn, he is not forced to be included.
This avoids dependency on the son unnecessarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وللابن عيال قيد به لأنه لو لم يكن له عيال لا يضم الأب إلى نفسه إذ لم يكفهما كسبه قال في الذخيرة وقال بعض العلماء: يجبر الابن على أن يدخل الأب في قوته إذا كان ما يصيب الابن من ذلك القوت يقيم بدنه ولا يضره إضراراً يمنعه من الكسب. وروي عن أبي يوسف أيضاً لأنه لو لم يفعل ضاع الأب إلا أن في ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا لا يجبر على ذلك لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ابدأ بنفسك ثم بمن تحول هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا كان الابن وحده فلو له زوجة وأولاد صغار وباقي المسألة بحالها، فالقاضي يجبره على أن يدخل الأب في كسبه ويجعله كأحد عياله ولا يجبره أن يعطي له شيئاً على حدة. والفرق أنه إذا أدخله في طعام عياله يقل لأن طعام الأربعة إذا فرق على الخمسة لا يتضرر كل واحد منهم ضرراً فاحشاً، أما إذا أدخل الواحد في طعام الواحد يتفاحش الضرر. ثم قال : هذا كله إذا كان الأب عاجزاً عن الكسب قوله : ( وقيد بفقرهم فقط) أي ولم يقيد بكونهم عاجزين عن الكسب قيل هو ظاهر الرواية لأن معنى الأذى في إيكاله إلى الكد والتعب أكثر منه في التأفيف المحرم بقوله تعالى فلا تقل لهما أف ولا تنهرهما ﴾ [الإسراء : ۲۳] كذا في فتح القدير. والقائل بأنه ظاهر الرواية صاحب الذخيرة، والضمير في قوله «ولأبويه) يعود إلى الإنسان المفهوم فأفاد بإطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين الذكر والأنثى. وفي الهداية : وهي على الذكور والإناث بالسوية في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح لأن المعنى يشملهما اهـ. وفي الخلاصة وبه يفتى. وفي فتح القدير : وهو الحق لتعلق الوجوب بالولاد وهو يشملهما بالسوية بخلاف غير الولاد لأن الوجوب علق فيه بالإرث اهـ. وفي الخانية : فإن كان للفقير ابنان أحدهما فائق في الغنى والآخر يملك نصاباً كانت النفقة عليهما على السواء، وكذا لو كان أحدهما مسلماً والآخر ذمياً فهي عليهما على السواء اهـ . وذكر في الذخيرة فيه اختلافاً وعزاماً في الخانية إلى مبسوط محمد، ونقل عن الحلواني أنه قال قال مشايخنا : هذا إذا تفاوتا في اليسار تفاوتاً يسيراً، أما إذا تفاوتا فيه تفاوتاً فاحشاً يجب أن يتفاوتا في قدر النفقة. وأشار بقوله «ولأبويه» إلى أن ما جميع وجب للمرأة يجب للأب والأم على الولد من طعام وشراب وكسوة وسكنى حتى الخادم . قال في الخانية : وكما يجب على الابن الموسر نفقة والده الفقير تجب عليه نفقة خادم الأب، امرأة كانت الخادم أو جارية، إذا كان الأب محتاجاً إلى من يخدمه اهـ. وفي الخلاصة يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه ولا يجبر الأب على نفقة زوجة ابنه وفي نفقات الحلواني قال : فيه روايتان، في رواية كما قلناه، وفي رواية إنما تجب نفقة زوجة الأب إذا كان الأب مريضاً أو به زمانة يحتاج إلى الخدمة، أما إذا كان صحيحاً فلا قال في المحيط فعلى هذا لا فرق بين الأب والابن فإن الابن إذا كان بهذه المثابة يجبر الأب على نفقة خادمه .اهـ. وظاهر ما في الذخيرة أن المذهب الرواية) أيده في الفتح في محل آخر بما في كافي الحاكم ولا يجبر الموسر على نفقة أحد من قرابته إذا كان رجلاً صحيحاً، وإن كان لا يقدر على الكسب إلا في الولد خاصة وفي الجد أب الأب إذا مات الولد فإني أجبر الولد على نفقته وإن كان صحيحاً اهـ. قال في الفتح وهذا جواب الرواية وهو يشيد قول شمس الأئمة السرخسي بخلاف الحلواني على ما قدمناه ا هـ . قوله : (يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه الخ) أي التي ليست أم الابن كما في الذخيرة قال الرملي الذي تحرر من المذهب أنه لا فرق بين الأب والابن في نفقة الخادم وأن الأب أو الابن إذا احتاج إلى خادم وجبت نفقته كما وجبت نفقة المخدوم لاحتياجه إليه فكان من جملة نفقته وإذا لم يحتج إليه فلا تجب عليه فاعلم ذلك واغتنمه فإنه كثير الوقوع والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم قوله : ( يجبر الأب على نفقة خادمة) قال الرملي :
His saying: 'and the son has dependents' is a qualification because if he had no dependents, he would not include the father with himself, since his earnings would not suffice both. He said in al-Dhakhira: Some scholars said: the son is forced to include the father in his food if what the son receives from that food sustains his body and does not harm him with harm that prevents him from earning. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf, because if he did not do so, the father would be lost. However, in the apparent narration from our companions, he is not forced to do so due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Begin with yourself, then with those you support.' What we have mentioned is when the son is alone. If he has a wife and young children, and the rest of the case is the same, then the judge forces him to include the father in his earnings and make him like one of his dependents, but does not force him to give him anything separately. The difference is that when he includes him in the food of his dependents, it becomes less, because the food of four when divided among five does not harm each one excessively. But when one person is added to the food of one, the harm becomes excessive. Then he said: This is all when the father is unable to earn. His saying: 'and he restricted it to their poverty only' meaning he did not restrict it to their inability to earn. It is said that this is the apparent narration because the meaning of harm in making him resort to toil and fatigue is greater than the harm in saying 'uff' which is forbidden by His saying: 'So do not say to them 'uff' and do not repel them' (al-Isra 23). This is from Fath al-Qadir. The one who says it is the apparent narration is the author of al-Dhakhira. The pronoun in His saying 'and for his parents' refers to the implied person, so its generality indicates that there is no difference between male and female. In al-Hidaya: It is upon males and females equally in the apparent narration, and that is correct because the meaning includes both. In al-Khulasa: And this is the fatwa. In Fath al-Qadir: It is the truth because the obligation is attached to birth, which includes both equally, unlike other than birth because the obligation there is attached to inheritance. In al-Khaniyya: If a poor man has two sons, one extremely rich and the other owns a nisab, the maintenance is upon them equally. Similarly, if one is Muslim and the other dhimmi, it is upon them equally. Al-Dhakhira mentioned a difference, and 'Azam in al-Khaniyya referred to Mabsut Muhammad, and narrated from al-Halwani that he said: Our scholars said: This is when they differ in wealth slightly, but if they differ excessively, they must differ in the amount of maintenance. He indicated by his saying 'and for his parents' that everything that is obligatory for the wife is obligatory for the father and mother upon the child, including food, drink, clothing, housing, and even the servant. He said in al-Khaniyya: Just as it is obligatory upon the wealthy son to support his poor father, so too is it obligatory upon him to support the father's servant, whether the servant is a woman or a slave girl, if the father is in need of someone to serve him. In al-Khulasa: The son is forced to support the wife of his father, but the father is not forced to support the wife of his son. In Nafaqat al-Halwani, he said: There are two narrations: in one narration as we said, and in another narration, the maintenance of the father's wife is only obligatory if the father is sick or disabled and needs service. But if he is healthy, it is not. He said in al-Muhit: On this basis, there is no difference between the father and the son, for if the son is in this condition, the father is forced to support his servant. The apparent meaning in al-Dhakhira is that the school is the narration supported by al-Fath in another place with what is in Kafi al-Hakim: A wealthy person is not forced to support any of his relatives if he is a healthy man, even if he is unable to earn, except specifically for the child, and for the grandfather (father's father) when the child dies, I force the child to support him even if he is healthy. He said in al-Fath: This is the answer of the narration, and it strengthens the saying of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi contrary to al-Halwani as we have mentioned. His saying: 'The son is forced to support the wife of his father' meaning who is not the mother of the son, as in al-Dhakhira. Al-Ramli said: What is established from the school is that there is no difference between the father and the son regarding the maintenance of the servant, and that if the father or son needs a servant, his maintenance is obligatory just as the maintenance of the served person is obligatory, due to his need for him, so it becomes part of his maintenance. If he does not need him, it is not obligatory. Know this and take advantage of it, for it occurs frequently, and Allah knows best. His saying: 'The father is forced to support his servant.' Al-Ramli said:
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings from the matn regarding maintenance when the son has dependents, and the obligations regarding a servant. It begins by explaining the qualification 'and the son has dependents' in the matn: if the son has no dependents, he is not required to include the father because his earnings would not suffice both. However, some scholars, including a narration from Abu Yusuf, hold that he should include the father if the son's food sustains him without excessive harm. But the zahir al-riwaya, based on the hadith 'Begin with yourself...', says the son is not forced alone, but if he has dependents, the judge forces him to include the father in his household as one of his dependents, not separately. The reason is that dividing food among more people does not cause excessive harm, but adding one to a single person's food does. This applies when the father cannot earn. Then the passage discusses the matn's phrase 'restricted to their poverty only' — meaning that the obligation of maintenance is tied to poverty, not inability to earn. This is the zahir al-riwaya because making the parent toil is a greater harm than saying 'uff'. The ruling applies equally to male and female parents, as obligations are based on birth. If there are multiple sons, they share equally even if one is much wealthier, unless the disparity is extreme, in which case they pay proportionally. Everything obligatory for a wife (food, drink, clothing, housing, servant) is also obligatory for parents. A son must support his father's servant if the father needs one, and similarly the father must support the son's servant if needed. There is a difference of opinion on whether a son must support his father's wife (stepmother): the main view says yes, but another narration restricts it to when the father is ill and needs service. The school's final position is that there is no difference between father and son regarding the servant's maintenance — it is obligatory when needed. The passage also notes that a wealthy person is not forced to support other relatives if he is healthy, except for his child and grandfather in specific cases.

Key Terms
ضم الأب (damm al-ab): Including the father in the son's household as one of his dependents for food and provisions.
التفاوت الفاحش (al-tafawut al-fahish): Extreme disparity in wealth between two children, requiring proportional (not equal) distribution of maintenance.
الزمانة (al-zamanah): Chronic illness or disability that prevents a person from working or serving themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition must be met for a son to be forced to include his poor father in his household?
A) The son must have surplus wealth beyond his own needs.
B) The son must have dependents of his own and the father must be unable to earn.
C) The father must request it in writing.
D) The son must be living with his wife only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the rights of the son's own household and the father by requiring inclusion only when it avoids excessive harm.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
advanced
10 min
Maintenance of Parents: Equal Sharing, Servant, and Stepmother
Expands the scope of parent maintenance and distribution rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for equal distribution of parent maintenance among children, identify when extreme disparity requires proportional sharing, and state the obligations regarding a servant and stepmother.

Core Idea
Parent maintenance is shared equally among children and includes food, clothing, housing, and a servant if needed.

This lesson expands on the matn's phrase 'restricted to their poverty only' and covers three important issues: the inclusion of a servant in maintenance, the obligation to support a father's wife (stepmother), and the distribution of maintenance among multiple children when one is significantly wealthier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of parent maintenance
The matn says the same obligations that exist for a wife's maintenance apply to parents: food, drink, clothing, housing, and even a servant if the parent needs one.
This is based on qiyas of the i'la (obligation) of birth.
2
Understand the rule of equal sharing among children
If a poor parent has multiple children, maintenance is on all of them equally, regardless of differences in wealth, according to the zahir al-riwaya.
This is because the obligation is tied to birth, not inheritance.
3
Recognize the exception of extreme disparity
Al-Halwani narrates from other scholars that if the children differ vastly in wealth (tafawut fahish), they should pay proportionally.
This is a dissenting view within the Hanafi school.
4
Learn about the servant's maintenance
If a parent needs a servant due to illness or disability (zamanah), the child must provide one, as it is part of the parent's maintenance.
This applies equally to father and son if either needs a servant.
5
Address the stepmother's maintenance
The son is forced to support his father's wife (stepmother) but the father is not forced to support his son's wife. There are two narrations on when stepmother maintenance is obligatory.
The discussion relies on al-Dhakhira and al-Ramli.

Source Text

يخدمه اهـ. وفي الخلاصة يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه ولا يجبر الأب على نفقة زوجة ابنه وفي نفقات الحلواني قال : فيه روايتان، في رواية كما قلناه، وفي رواية إنما تجب نفقة زوجة الأب إذا كان الأب مريضاً أو به زمانة يحتاج إلى الخدمة، أما إذا كان صحيحاً فلا قال في المحيط فعلى هذا لا فرق بين الأب والابن فإن الابن إذا كان بهذه المثابة يجبر الأب على نفقة خادمه .اهـ. وظاهر ما في الذخيرة أن المذهب الرواية) أيده في الفتح في محل آخر بما في كافي الحاكم ولا يجبر الموسر على نفقة أحد من قرابته إذا كان رجلاً صحيحاً، وإن كان لا يقدر على الكسب إلا في الولد خاصة وفي الجد أب الأب إذا مات الولد فإني أجبر الولد على نفقته وإن كان صحيحاً اهـ. قال في الفتح وهذا جواب الرواية وهو يشيد قول شمس الأئمة السرخسي بخلاف الحلواني على ما قدمناه ا هـ . قوله : (يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه الخ) أي التي ليست أم الابن كما في الذخيرة قال الرملي الذي تحرر من المذهب أنه لا فرق بين الأب والابن في نفقة الخادم وأن الأب أو الابن إذا احتاج إلى خادم وجبت نفقته كما وجبت نفقة المخدوم لاحتياجه إليه فكان من جملة نفقته وإذا لم يحتج إليه فلا تجب عليه فاعلم ذلك واغتنمه فإنه كثير الوقوع والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم قوله : ( يجبر الأب على نفقة خادمة) قال الرملي :
His saying: 'and the son has dependents' is a qualification because if he had no dependents, he would not include the father with himself, since his earnings would not suffice both. He said in al-Dhakhira: Some scholars said: the son is forced to include the father in his food if what the son receives from that food sustains his body and does not harm him with harm that prevents him from earning. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf, because if he did not do so, the father would be lost. However, in the apparent narration from our companions, he is not forced to do so due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Begin with yourself, then with those you support.' What we have mentioned is when the son is alone. If he has a wife and young children, and the rest of the case is the same, then the judge forces him to include the father in his earnings and make him like one of his dependents, but does not force him to give him anything separately. The difference is that when he includes him in the food of his dependents, it becomes less, because the food of four when divided among five does not harm each one excessively. But when one person is added to the food of one, the harm becomes excessive. Then he said: This is all when the father is unable to earn. His saying: 'and he restricted it to their poverty only' meaning he did not restrict it to their inability to earn. It is said that this is the apparent narration because the meaning of harm in making him resort to toil and fatigue is greater than the harm in saying 'uff' which is forbidden by His saying: 'So do not say to them 'uff' and do not repel them' (al-Isra 23). This is from Fath al-Qadir. The one who says it is the apparent narration is the author of al-Dhakhira. The pronoun in His saying 'and for his parents' refers to the implied person, so its generality indicates that there is no difference between male and female. In al-Hidaya: It is upon males and females equally in the apparent narration, and that is correct because the meaning includes both. In al-Khulasa: And this is the fatwa. In Fath al-Qadir: It is the truth because the obligation is attached to birth, which includes both equally, unlike other than birth because the obligation there is attached to inheritance. In al-Khaniyya: If a poor man has two sons, one extremely rich and the other owns a nisab, the maintenance is upon them equally. Similarly, if one is Muslim and the other dhimmi, it is upon them equally. Al-Dhakhira mentioned a difference, and 'Azam in al-Khaniyya referred to Mabsut Muhammad, and narrated from al-Halwani that he said: Our scholars said: This is when they differ in wealth slightly, but if they differ excessively, they must differ in the amount of maintenance. He indicated by his saying 'and for his parents' that everything that is obligatory for the wife is obligatory for the father and mother upon the child, including food, drink, clothing, housing, and even the servant. He said in al-Khaniyya: Just as it is obligatory upon the wealthy son to support his poor father, so too is it obligatory upon him to support the father's servant, whether the servant is a woman or a slave girl, if the father is in need of someone to serve him. In al-Khulasa: The son is forced to support the wife of his father, but the father is not forced to support the wife of his son. In Nafaqat al-Halwani, he said: There are two narrations: in one narration as we said, and in another narration, the maintenance of the father's wife is only obligatory if the father is sick or disabled and needs service. But if he is healthy, it is not. He said in al-Muhit: On this basis, there is no difference between the father and the son, for if the son is in this condition, the father is forced to support his servant. The apparent meaning in al-Dhakhira is that the school is the narration supported by al-Fath in another place with what is in Kafi al-Hakim: A wealthy person is not forced to support any of his relatives if he is a healthy man, even if he is unable to earn, except specifically for the child, and for the grandfather (father's father) when the child dies, I force the child to support him even if he is healthy. He said in al-Fath: This is the answer of the narration, and it strengthens the saying of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi contrary to al-Halwani as we have mentioned. His saying: 'The son is forced to support the wife of his father' meaning who is not the mother of the son, as in al-Dhakhira. Al-Ramli said: What is established from the school is that there is no difference between the father and the son regarding the maintenance of the servant, and that if the father or son needs a servant, his maintenance is obligatory just as the maintenance of the served person is obligatory, due to his need for him, so it becomes part of his maintenance. If he does not need him, it is not obligatory. Know this and take advantage of it, for it occurs frequently, and Allah knows best. His saying: 'The father is forced to support his servant.' Al-Ramli said:
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings from the matn regarding maintenance when the son has dependents, and the obligations regarding a servant. It begins by explaining the qualification 'and the son has dependents' in the matn: if the son has no dependents, he is not required to include the father because his earnings would not suffice both. However, some scholars, including a narration from Abu Yusuf, hold that he should include the father if the son's food sustains him without excessive harm. But the zahir al-riwaya, based on the hadith 'Begin with yourself...', says the son is not forced alone, but if he has dependents, the judge forces him to include the father in his household as one of his dependents, not separately. The reason is that dividing food among more people does not cause excessive harm, but adding one to a single person's food does. This applies when the father cannot earn. Then the passage discusses the matn's phrase 'restricted to their poverty only' — meaning that the obligation of maintenance is tied to poverty, not inability to earn. This is the zahir al-riwaya because making the parent toil is a greater harm than saying 'uff'. The ruling applies equally to male and female parents, as obligations are based on birth. If there are multiple sons, they share equally even if one is much wealthier, unless the disparity is extreme, in which case they pay proportionally. Everything obligatory for a wife (food, drink, clothing, housing, servant) is also obligatory for parents. A son must support his father's servant if the father needs one, and similarly the father must support the son's servant if needed. There is a difference of opinion on whether a son must support his father's wife (stepmother): the main view says yes, but another narration restricts it to when the father is ill and needs service. The school's final position is that there is no difference between father and son regarding the servant's maintenance — it is obligatory when needed. The passage also notes that a wealthy person is not forced to support other relatives if he is healthy, except for his child and grandfather in specific cases.

Key Terms
ضم الأب (damm al-ab): Including the father in the son's household as one of his dependents for food and provisions.
التفاوت الفاحش (al-tafawut al-fahish): Extreme disparity in wealth between two children, requiring proportional (not equal) distribution of maintenance.
الزمانة (al-zamanah): Chronic illness or disability that prevents a person from working or serving themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general rule when multiple children are responsible for a parent's maintenance?
A) The wealthiest child pays the full amount.
B) All children share equally regardless of wealth disparity.
C) Each child pays a fixed percentage of their income.
D) Only male children pay.

Key Takeaway
Parent maintenance in the Hanafi school is comprehensive and shared equally among children, with a servant included if necessary.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Basis of Maintenance for Parents: Poverty, Not Earning Capacity
Establishes maintenance basis: poverty, not earning capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for parents, explain why poverty alone is the basis, and apply it equally to all children.

Core Idea
Maintenance for parents is wajib solely due to their poverty, regardless of earning capacity, and it is equal for all children.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation to support one's parents is not triggered by their inability to earn, but by their actual poverty. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq uses istihsan based on the Quranic verse prohibiting even 'uff' to parents. You will see why the son must earn and support his father if both can earn, and why daughters share equally in this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine that maintenance for parents is wajib (obligatory) and note its basis: the parent's poverty.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic proof (al-Isra 17:23) and note the author's use of istihsan.
The verse prohibits even 'uff' to parents.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand why the verse supports wujub: making parents work is a greater harm than 'uff', so maintenance is obligatory to prevent it.
4
Note the authority and ikhtilaf
Confirm that this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah and that it is the mufta bihi. Note that other schools may differ on the equality of children.
Al-Khulasah says 'bi hi yufata'; Fath al-Qadir says 'huwa al-haqq'.
5
Apply the ruling to specific cases
Consider the examples given: even if one child is very wealthy and another only has a nisab, both contribute equally; similarly, Muslim and dhimmi children are equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كان الأب كسوباً لأنه غني باعتبار الكسب فلا ضرورة في إيجاب النفقة على الغير، وإذا كان الابن قادراً على الكسب لا تجب نفقته على الأب فلو كان كل منهما كسوباً يجب أن يكتسب الابن وينفق على الأب، فالمعتبر في إيحاب نفقة الوالدين مجرد الفقر . قيل : هو ظاهر الرواية لأن معنی الأذى في إيكاله إلى الكد والتعب أكثر منه في التأفيف المحرم بقوله تعالى فلا تقل لهما أف ولا تنهرهما ﴾ [الإسراء : ۲۳] كذا في فتح القدير. والقائل بأنه ظاهر الرواية صاحب الذخيرة، والضمير في قوله «ولأبويه) يعود إلى الإنسان المفهوم فأفاد بإطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين الذكر والأنثى. وفي الهداية : وهي على الذكور والإناث بالسوية في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح لأن المعنى يشملهما اهـ. وفي الخلاصة وبه يفتى. وفي فتح القدير : وهو الحق لتعلق الوجوب بالولاد وهو يشملهما بالسوية بخلاف غير الولاد لأن الوجوب علق فيه بالإرث اهـ. وفي الخانية : فإن كان للفقير ابنان أحدهما فائق في الغنى والآخر يملك نصاباً كانت النفقة عليهما على السواء، وكذا لو كان أحدهما مسلماً والآخر ذمياً فهي عليهما على السواء اهـ .
If the father is capable of earning, he is considered wealthy by virtue of earning, so there is no necessity to impose maintenance on another. If the son is capable of earning, his maintenance is not obligatory upon the father. If both are capable of earning, the son must earn and spend on the father. So the consideration in imposing maintenance for parents is merely poverty. It is said: This is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) because the harm in making them endure toil and fatigue is greater than the harm in saying 'uff' which is prohibited by His statement 'So do not say to them 'uff' and do not repel them' (al-Isra: 23). Thus in Fath al-Qadir. The one who says it is Zahir al-Riwayah is the author of al-Dhakhirah. The pronoun in 'wal-abawayhi' refers to the understood person, so by its generality it indicates there is no difference between male and female. In al-Hidayah: 'And it is upon males and females equally in Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the correct view because the meaning includes both.' In al-Khulasah: 'And by it fatwa is given.' In Fath al-Qadir: 'It is the truth because the obligation is attached to birth, which includes both equally, unlike other than birth, because obligation there is attached to inheritance.' In al-Khaniyyah: 'If a poor person has two sons, one extremely wealthy and the other possessing a nisab, maintenance is upon both equally. Similarly, if one is Muslim and the other a dhimmi, it is upon both equally.'
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It establishes the key principle that the obligation of maintenance for parents is based solely on their poverty, not on the parent's ability to earn. The author argues that if the father is capable of earning, he is considered wealthy in that regard, so there is no need to oblige the son. Conversely, if the son can earn, the father is not obliged to support him. If both are capable, the son, being the child, must earn and support the father. The proof is an istihsan (juristic preference) based on the Quranic verse prohibiting even saying 'uff' to parents. The harm of making parents work is greater than saying 'uff', hence maintenance is obligatory upon the child when needed. The author confirms that this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah, as stated by the author of al-Dhakhirah. Furthermore, the obligation is equal for male and female children, as the term 'walad' includes both. This is supported by al-Hidayah, al-Khulasah, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Khaniyyah, which state that even if one child is very wealthy and the other only has a nisab, both contribute equally. Even if one is Muslim and the other a dhimmi, they are equal in obligation.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, housing, and necessities, obligatory upon a person for certain relatives.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most authoritative in the Hanafi school.
الولاد (al-wilad): Birth or filiation; the biological relationship that triggers maintenance obligation for parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on what basis is the obligation of maintenance for parents determined?
A) The parent's ability to earn
B) The parent's poverty alone
C) The child's wealth
D) The parent's age

Key Takeaway
Maintenance for parents in the Hanafi school is wajib based solely on the parent's poverty, and it is equally incumbent on all children, regardless of their relative wealth or religion.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Maintenance: Disparity, Servant, and Father's Wife
Discusses intra-Hanafi disputes on maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conflicting narrations regarding the maintenance of a stepmother and state the mufta bihi ruling for the maintenance of a servant according to al-Ramli.

Core Idea
Maintenance obligations are need-based: servant depends on need; stepmother's maintenance is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into several intra-Hanafi disputes concerning the scope of maintenance (nafaqah). The author first examines whether children must contribute equally when there is a vast disparity in their wealth, then discusses whether a servant's maintenance is included, and finally addresses the obligation to maintain a father's wife (stepmother). The passage resolves these issues by weighing conflicting narrations and statements from leading Hanafi authorities, culminating in al-Ramli's settled view that need, not relationship, is the decisive factor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Issues
Read the passage and isolate the three distinct rulings: (1) disparity in contribution, (2) servant for parent, (3) stepmother's maintenance.
Each issue has its own set of conflicting views.
2
Extract the Conflicting Views
For each issue, note the two (or more) positions. For disparity: equal vs. proportional (al-Halwani). For servant: obligatory if needed vs. not? (implicit). For stepmother: always vs. only if father sick.
Sources: al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, al-Ramli.
3
Trace Authority Chain
Identify who said what: al-Halwani reports from his shaykhs; al-Sarakhsi opposes; al-Fath supports al-Sarakhsi; al-Ramli gives the settled view.
Note the use of 'ظاهر ما في الذخيرة' and 'الذي تحرر من المذهب'.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
State the operative ruling for fatwa: for servant—obligatory if needed for either father or son; for stepmother—the first narration (always obligatory) appears stronger, but al-Ramli emphasizes need.
Al-Ramli: 'لا فرق بين الأب والابن في نفقة الخادم'.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a case: a wealthy son has a healthy father who can care for himself but has an elderly stepmother. Is the son compelled to maintain her? According to the first narration, yes; according to the second, no. Mufta bihi? The passage leans toward the first.
Apply the principle of need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في الذخيرة فيه اختلافاً وعزاماً في الخانية إلى مبسوط محمد، ونقل عن الحلواني أنه قال قال مشايخنا : هذا إذا تفاوتا في اليسار تفاوتاً يسيراً، أما إذا تفاوتا فيه تفاوتاً فاحشاً يجب أن يتفاوتا في قدر النفقة. وأشار بقوله «ولأبويه» إلى أن ما جميع وجب للمرأة يجب للأب والأم على الولد من طعام وشراب وكسوة وسكنى حتى الخادم . قال في الخانية : وكما يجب على الابن الموسر نفقة والده الفقير تجب عليه نفقة خادم الأب، امرأة كانت الخادم أو جارية، إذا كان الأب محتاجاً إلى من يخدمه اهـ. وفي الخلاصة يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه ولا يجبر الأب على نفقة زوجة ابنه وفي نفقات الحلواني قال : فيه روايتان، في رواية كما قلناه، وفي رواية إنما تجب نفقة زوجة الأب إذا كان الأب مريضاً أو به زمانة يحتاج إلى الخدمة، أما إذا كان صحيحاً فلا قال في المحيط فعلى هذا لا فرق بين الأب والابن فإن الابن إذا كان بهذه المثابة يجبر الأب على نفقة خادمه .اهـ. وظاهر ما في الذخيرة أن المذهب الرواية) أيده في الفتح في محل آخر بما في كافي الحاكم ولا يجبر الموسر على نفقة أحد من قرابته إذا كان رجلاً صحيحاً، وإن كان لا يقدر على الكسب إلا في الولد خاصة وفي الجد أب الأب إذا مات الولد فإني أجبر الولد على نفقته وإن كان صحيحاً اهـ. قال في الفتح وهذا جواب الرواية وهو يشيد قول شمس الأئمة السرخسي بخلاف الحلواني على ما قدمناه ا هـ . قوله : (يجبر الابن على نفقة زوجة أبيه الخ) أي التي ليست أم الابن كما في الذخيرة قال الرملي الذي تحرر من المذهب أنه لا فرق بين الأب والابن في نفقة الخادم وأن الأب أو الابن إذا احتاج إلى خادم وجبت نفقته كما وجبت نفقة المخدوم لاحتياجه إليه فكان من جملة نفقته وإذا لم يحتج إليه فلا تجب عليه فاعلم ذلك واغتنمه فإنه كثير الوقوع والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم
And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah that there is a difference of opinion, and it is reported in al-Khaniyyah from the Mabsut of Muhammad, and it is transmitted from al-Halwani that he said: 'Our shaykhs said: This is when they differ in wealth by a small difference. But if they differ in it by a large difference, they must differ in the amount of maintenance.' And he indicated by his statement 'wal-abawayhi' that everything that is obligatory for a woman is obligatory for the father and mother upon the child, of food, drink, clothing, and housing, even the servant. He said in al-Khaniyyah: 'Just as it is obligatory upon the wealthy son to provide maintenance for his poor father, so too is the maintenance of the father's servant obligatory upon him, whether the servant be a woman or a slave girl, if the father is in need of someone to serve him.' In al-Khulasah: 'The son is compelled to provide maintenance for his father's wife, and the father is not compelled to provide maintenance for his son's wife.' And in Nafaqat al-Halwani, he said: 'There are two narrations. In one narration, as we said. In another narration, the maintenance of the father's wife is only obligatory if the father is sick or has a chronic illness requiring service. As for if he is healthy, then no.' He said in al-Muhit: 'On this basis, there is no difference between the father and the son, for if the son is in this situation, the father is compelled to provide maintenance for his servant.' The apparent from al-Dhakhirah is that the madhhab is the first narration, supported in al-Fath in another place by what is in Kafi al-Hakim: 'A wealthy person is not compelled to provide maintenance for any of his relatives if he is a healthy man, even if he is unable to earn, except specifically for his child, and for the grandfather (father's father) if the child dies, for I compel the child to provide his maintenance even if he is healthy.' He said in al-Fath: 'This is the answer of the narration, and it supports the statement of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi contrary to al-Halwani, as we have mentioned.' His statement: 'The son is compelled to provide maintenance for his father's wife' means the one who is not the son's mother, as in al-Dhakhirah. Al-Ramli said: 'What is settled from the madhhab is that there is no difference between the father and the son regarding the maintenance of the servant, and that if the father or the son needs a servant, his maintenance is obligatory as the maintenance of the one being served, because of his need for him, so it becomes part of his maintenance. If he does not need him, it is not obligatory upon him. Know this and take it, for it frequently occurs. And Allah Most High knows best.'
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute and rulings on maintenance. First, there is a dispute about whether children must contribute equally if they differ vastly in wealth. The default is equality, but al-Halwani reports from his shaykhs that if the disparity is huge, the contribution should be proportional. However, the author does not definitively choose, but mentions the view of al-Dhakhirah supporting the first narration (equality) and al-Fath supporting al-Sarakhsi against al-Halwani. Next, the passage clarifies that maintenance includes a servant (khaddam) for the father if he needs one, as stated in al-Khaniyyah. Then it discusses the father's wife (not the son's mother). There is a dispute: some say the son must always maintain her, while another narration limits it to when the father is sick and needs service. The author inclines to the first view, as per al-Dhakhirah and supported by Kafi al-Hakim, which states that a healthy person is not compelled except for his child and in certain cases. Al-Ramli settles that there is no difference between father and son regarding maintenance of a servant: if either needs a servant, it is obligatory; otherwise not.

Key Terms
الخادم (al-khaddam): Servant or attendant whose maintenance may be obligatory if the person being supported needs one.
زوجة الأب (zawjat al-ab): The father's wife who is not the son's mother, whose maintenance may be obligatory upon the son under certain conditions.
التفاوت الفاحش (al-tafawut al-fahish): Gross disparity in wealth that may justify unequal contribution among children for parental maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli's settled view in the passage, when is maintenance of a servant (khaddam) obligatory for either the father or the son?
A) Always, if they are old
B) Only if they are sick
C) When they need a servant
D) Only for the father, not the son

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi maintenance law, the servant's upkeep is need-based, and the father's wife's maintenance is generally obligatory but subject to a minority conditional view.

The Basis of Maintenance: Closeness and Partiality
Principle of maintenance based on closeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that maintenance for parents and children is based on closeness and partiality, and apply it to determine obligation in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Maintenance for parents and children is based on closeness, not inheritance.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a foundational principle in Hanafi maintenance law: the obligation to support one's parents and children stems from the closeness of kinship (qurb) and the idea that they are part of one's lineage (juz'iyyah), not from any right of inheritance. The author reinforces this by providing examples where a closer relative, even if not an heir, takes priority over a more distant heir. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly determining who must provide support in a family.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Locate the statement 'إنما وهو القرب والجزئية' – this is the core rule: maintenance obligation for parents and children is based solely on closeness and partiality, not on inheritance.
The author explicitly says inheritance is not considered.
2
Analyze the examples given
Examine the examples: son vs. grandson, daughter vs. grandson, daughter's child vs. son's child. Identify which relative is closer and who is obligated according to the principle.
Note that in each case, the closer relative bears the maintenance, regardless of inheritance.
3
Recognize the exception for equal closeness
When relatives are equally close (e.g., two sons), the text mentions that inheritance may be used to apportion maintenance. This is a secondary consideration.
The primary rule still stands; inheritance is only a tiebreaker.
4
Contrast with contradictory rulings
Identify passages that seem to incorporate inheritance directly (e.g., grandfather and grandson, mother and uncle). Note these contradictions for further study.
These will be addressed in a subsequent lesson.

Source Text

محمد بالوجوب عدم وجوب نفقة امرأة الأب أو جاريته أو أم ولده حيث لم يكن بالأب علة، وأن القول مطلقاً إنما هو رواية عن أبي يوسف. وفي الذخيرة أيضاً: ثم إذا قضى القاضي بالنفقة على الولدين للأب فأبى أحدهما أن يعطي للأب ما يجب عليه فالقاضي يأمر الآخر بأن يعطي كل النفقة ثم يرجع على الأخ بحصته .اهـ ومراد المصنف من إيجاب نفقة الأم على الولد إذا لم تكن متزوجة لأنها على الزوج كبنته المراهقة إذا زوجها صارت نفقتها على زوجها، وقدمنا أن الزوج لو كان معسراً فإن الابن يؤمر بأن يقرضها ثم يرجع عليه إذا أيسر، وقد صرح به في الذخيرة هنا أيضاً قال: فإن أبى الابن أن يقرضها النفقة فرض لها عليه النفقة وتؤخذ منه وتدفع إليها لأن الزوج المعسر بمنزلة الميت. وأشار المصنف بقوله «ولأبويه» إلى أن الاعتبار في وجوب نفقة الوالدين والمولودين إنما وهو القرب والجزئية ولا يعتبر الميراث قالوا: وإذا استويا في القرب تجب على من له نوع رجحان، وإذا لم يكن لأحدهما رجحان فحينئذ تجب النفقة بقدر الميراث فإن كان للفقير ولد وابن ابن موسرين فالنفقة على الولد لأنه أقرب، وإذا كانت له بنت وابن ابن فالنفقة على البنت خاصة، وإن كان الميراث المختار من أنه يؤمر بالإنفاق عليها ويرجع على الزوج إذا أيسر. ثم راجعت الذخيرة فرأيته ذكر تأويل ما هنا فقال : قالوا والمراد من الفرض المذكور في هذا هو الإجبار على الإقراض لا الفرض بطريق الإيجاب ا.هـ. وبه اندفعت المخالفة . قوله : (إنما هو القرب والجزئية وعليه فلو كان له ابن بنت أو بنت بنت وابن ابن فالنفقة على ولد البنت وإن كان الميراث للابن الثاني، وبه صرح وقوله تجب على من له نوع رجحان» أي كابن ابن وبنت بنت فهي على ابن الابن لرجحانه رملي أي لرجحانه بكونه هو الوارث لكن هذا الفرع يحتاج إلى نص عليه من كلامهم وإلا فهو مخالف لما يأتي قريباً من الفروع الدالة على عدم اعتبار الإرث أصلاً في نفقة الأصول على الفروع. قال في أحكام الصغار : إذا كان له بنت بنت وابن بنت موسران وأخ موسر فالنفقة على أولاد أولاده لأن في باب النفقة يعتبر الأقرب فالأقرب ولا يعتبر الإرث في الأولاد ا . وقال بعده أيضاً : نفقته على أولاد البنات يستوي فيها الذكر والأنثى ولا عبرة للإرث في الأولاد، وإنما يعتبر القرب حتى لو كان له بنت وابن ابن فالنفقة على البنت ا هـ تأمل. قوله : (ولا يعتبر الميراث) يخالفه ما سيأتي قبيل قوله وصح بيع قريباً قوله : (بقدر الميراث) يرد عليه الابن والبنت فإنه لا رجحان فيهما. أن النفقة عليهما سوية قوله : ( فالنفقة على ولد البنت هي: مع
Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds obligation? Non-obligation of maintenance for the father's wife, his slave-girl, or his umm walad if the father has no illness, and that the absolute statement is only a narration from Abu Yusuf. And in al-Dhakhirah also: 'Then if the judge rules for maintenance upon the two sons for the father, and one of them refuses to give the father what is due, the judge orders the other to give all the maintenance and then reclaim his brother's share.' The intent of the author regarding the obligation of maintenance of the mother upon the child if she is not married, because it is upon the husband like his adult daughter when she marries, her maintenance becomes upon her husband. We have already stated that if the husband is insolvent, the son is ordered to lend her the maintenance and then reclaim from the husband when he becomes wealthy, as explicitly stated in al-Dhakhirah here also. He said: 'If the son refuses to lend her the maintenance, it is assessed as maintenance upon him and taken from him and given to her, because an insolvent husband is like a dead person.' The author indicated by his statement 'wal-abawayhi' that the consideration in the obligation of maintenance for parents and children is only closeness and partiality, and inheritance is not considered. They said: 'If they are equal in closeness, it is obligatory upon the one who has some weight (tarjihan). If neither has weight, then maintenance is according to the share of inheritance.' So if a poor person has a son and a son's son (grandson) who are wealthy, maintenance is upon the son because he is closer. If he has a daughter and a son's son, maintenance is upon the daughter alone, even if inheritance is between them... The servant as already mentioned. His statement: 'It is explicitly stated in al-Dhakhirah here also...' I say: We have already mentioned at the statement of the matn 'and it is not differentiated by his inability' that the statement of al-Dhakhirah here imposing maintenance upon him contradicts what he mentioned there from Sharh al-Mukhtar that he is ordered to spend on her and reclaim from the husband when he becomes wealthy. Then I consulted al-Dhakhirah and found that he mentioned an interpretation of what is here, saying: 'They said: The intended meaning of the imposition mentioned here is compulsion to lend, not imposition by way of obligation.' Thus the contradiction is removed. His statement: 'It is only closeness and partiality. Accordingly, if someone has a daughter's son or a daughter's daughter and a son's son, maintenance is upon the child of the daughter even if inheritance is for the second son, and he explicitly stated it.' And his statement: 'It is obligatory upon the one who has some weight' meaning like a son's son and a daughter's daughter, it is upon the son's son for his weight (tarjih). Al-Ramli: 'For his weight being that he is the heir. But this branch needs textual evidence from their statements, otherwise it contradicts what comes shortly of branches indicating that inheritance is not considered at all in maintenance of ancestors upon descendants.' He said in Ahkam al-Sighar: 'If someone has a daughter's daughter and a daughter's son who are wealthy, and a wealthy brother, maintenance is upon his grandchildren because in the chapter of maintenance, the closest is considered, and inheritance is not considered in children.' And he also said after it: 'His maintenance is upon the daughters' children, equally between male and female, and no consideration is given to inheritance among children. Only closeness is considered, so even if he has a daughter and a son's son, maintenance is upon the daughter.' Ponder. His statement: 'Inheritance is not considered' is contradicted by what will come shortly before his statement: 'It is valid to sell the property of his son'; he has a mother and a wealthy paternal uncle, maintenance is upon them in thirds. He has a mother and two fathers (paternal and maternal)? Thus the mother is closer than the grandfather. Similarly, it is contradicted by his statement coming shortly: 'If he has a grandfather and a son's son, maintenance is upon them according to the share of their inheritance.' And similarly what we will mention shortly. His statement: 'According to inheritance' is contradicted by the son and the daughter, for there is no weight (tarjih) between them, yet maintenance is equal upon them. His statement: 'Maintenance is upon the child of the daughter' is: with?
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage deals with the fundamental principles governing maintenance obligations among relatives. The author begins by clarifying the ruling on the father's wife, slave-girl, or umm walad: according to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), maintenance is not obligatory if the father is healthy; only Abu Yusuf's narration obligates it absolutely. Then, he discusses the mother's maintenance: if she is not married, the son must support her; if she is married and her husband is insolvent, the son is to lend her maintenance and reclaim from the husband later, as stated in al-Dhakhirah. The key principle introduced is that maintenance for parents and children is based on closeness (qurb) and partiality (juz'iyyah), not inheritance (mirath). However, when relatives are equally close, then inheritance distribution may be considered. The text then provides examples: a son is closer than a grandson, a daughter takes priority over a grandson, but a daughter's child takes priority over a son's child? The passage cites conflicting rulings: some say maintenance is based on closeness alone (e.g., Ahkam al-Sighar: daughter's children over brother), while other rulings incorporate inheritance (e.g., between grandfather and grandson, or between mother and paternal uncle). The author points out these apparent contradictions and calls for careful examination. The passage ends abruptly with an incomplete sentence, suggesting the text continues onto the next page. Overall, it highlights the complexity in Hanafi jurisprudence regarding the interplay of qurb, juz'iyyah, and mirath in determining maintenance obligations.

Key Terms
القرب والجزئية (al-qurb wa al-juz'iyyah): Closeness of relation and partiality (being a part of the lineage) as the primary basis for maintenance obligation, overriding inheritance.
الميراث (al-mirath): Inheritance; the transmission of property from a deceased person. In this context, it is sometimes considered for apportioning maintenance among equally close relatives.
الرجحان (al-tarjih): Weight or preference; a factor that tips the obligation towards one relative over another when they are equally close, such as being an heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is obligated to provide maintenance for a needy mother: her son or her grandson (son's son), assuming both are wealthy?
A) The grandson, because he inherits more
B) The son, because he is closer
C) Both equally, because they are equally related
D) Neither, because the mother should support herself

Key Takeaway
The primary basis for maintenance in Hanafi law is closeness and partiality, not inheritance.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
advanced
10 min
The Role of Inheritance in Maintenance: Internal Hanafi Disputes
Conflicting rulings on inheritance in maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the consideration of inheritance in maintenance obligations and explain the tarjih mechanism used to reconcile conflicting rulings.

Core Idea
When relatives are equally close, inheritance shares may determine maintenance, creating apparent contradictions.

While the primary basis for maintenance is closeness, the Hanafi school acknowledges that when two relatives are equally close, inheritance can serve as a tiebreaker. However, this leads to several apparent contradictions within the madhhab, as different scholars and texts apply this rule inconsistently. This lesson examines those conflicting rulings and the attempts to reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
Review the principle of inheritance as a secondary factor
Recall from the previous lesson that when relatives are equally close, maintenance is apportioned according to inheritance shares. This is stated in the passage: 'وإذا لم يكن لأحدهما رجحان فحينئذ تجب النفقة بقدر الميراث'.
This is the exception to the primary rule.
2
Identify conflicting rulings in the passage
The passage lists several cases that seem to contradict the principle: e.g., mother and uncle maintenance in thirds, grandfather and grandson according to inheritance, and the case of son and daughter where maintenance is equal despite no tarjih.
Note that in the son/daughter case, there is no tarjih but maintenance is equal, not by inheritance.
3
Understand the nature of the ikhtilaf
The contradictions arise from different narrations and interpretations within the Hanafi school. Some early scholars (e.g., Abu Yusuf) gave more weight to inheritance, while others (e.g., Muhammad al-Shaybani) emphasized closeness.
This is a legitimate intra-madhhab difference.
4
Apply tarjih (preference) to determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi jurists, like the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, attempt to reconcile the conflicting rulings. The primary principle (closeness) is upheld; inheritance is only considered when closeness is exactly equal and no other tarjih exists.
Tarjih based on being an heir is one form of weight.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Maintenance of Father's Wife and Mother's Maintenance
Ruling on non-obligation of son to support father's wife, and mother's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a son is obligated to provide maintenance for his father's wife and for his mother, and identify the special ruling from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Son not obligated to support father's wife unless father incapacitated; mother's maintenance falls on son if she has no solvent husband.

Maintenance obligations are central to family law. This passage clarifies two specific cases: a father's wife (including slave girls and umm walad) and a mother. The default assumption might be that children must support all relatives, but Hanafi fiqh draws careful distinctions based on marital ties and financial ability. Let us examine the rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct cases
The passage addresses two scenarios: maintenance of the father's wife (and his slave-girl/umm walad) and maintenance of the mother. Note the different rulings.
The father's wife is not a blood relative, whereas the mother is.
2
Analyze the father's wife case
The default ruling is that a son is not obligated to provide maintenance for his father's wife, slave-girl, or umm walad, unless the father has an infirmity. This ruling is traced to a special narration from Imam Abu Yusuf (considered Nawadir).
The general Hanafi position is consistent with this.
3
Analyze the mother's maintenance case
If the mother is married, her maintenance is on her husband. If she is not married or her husband is insolvent, the obligation shifts to her son. The son is first asked to lend her the money; if he refuses, the qadi can compel him to pay directly.
The insolvent husband is treated like a deceased person for this purpose.
4
Distinguish the underlying principles
The father's wife is not a blood relative and does not have a direct maintenance claim on the son. The mother's claim is stronger because of the direct maternal bond. Also, the husband's obligation takes precedence over the son's.
Maintenance obligations follow both marriage and lineage, with priority to the spouse.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
In real life, a son may face requests from a stepmother or his own mother. This ruling provides clear guidance: a stepmother has no claim unless the father is unable; the mother has a claim only if she is without a capable husband.
The son's duty is secondary and conditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب النفقة بالوجوب عدم وجوب نفقة امرأة الأب أو جاريته أو أم ولده حيث لم يكن بالأب علة، وأن القول مطلقاً إنما هو رواية عن أبي يوسف. وفي الذخيرة أيضاً: ثم إذا قضى القاضي بالنفقة على الولدين للأب فأبى أحدهما أن يعطي للأب ما يجب عليه فالقاضي يأمر الآخر بأن يعطي كل النفقة ثم يرجع على الأخ بحصته .اهـ ومراد المصنف من إيجاب نفقة الأم على الولد إذا لم تكن متزوجة لأنها على الزوج كبنته المراهقة إذا زوجها صارت نفقتها على زوجها، وقدمنا أن الزوج لو كان معسراً فإن الابن يؤمر بأن يقرضها ثم يرجع عليه إذا أيسر، وقد صرح به في الذخيرة هنا أيضاً قال: فإن أبى الابن أن يقرضها النفقة فرض لها عليه النفقة وتؤخذ منه وتدفع إليها لأن الزوج المعسر بمنزلة الميت.
The book of divorce, chapter of maintenance: The obligation is that maintenance for the father's wife, his slave-girl, or his umm walad is not obligatory when the father has no infirmity, and that the statement absolutely is only a narration from Abu Yusuf. In al-Dhakhira also: Then if the qadi rules maintenance on the two sons for the father and one refuses to give the father what is due on him, the qadi orders the other to give all the maintenance then he recovers his share from the brother. The author's intent from making the mother's maintenance obligatory on the child is when she is not married, because it is on the husband, like his grown-up daughter when she is married, her maintenance becomes on her husband. We have already stated that if the husband is insolvent, the son is ordered to lend her maintenance and then recover it from the husband when he becomes wealthy. It is stated in al-Dhakhira here also: He said: If the son refuses to lend her the maintenance, it is prescribed for him as maintenance and taken from him and given to her because the insolvent husband is like a dead person.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It addresses two specific maintenance issues. First, a son is not obligated to provide maintenance for his father's wife, slave-girl, or umm walad unless the father himself is incapacitated. This ruling is attributed to Abu Yusuf as a unique narration. Second, regarding a mother's maintenance, the default obligation is on her husband if she is married. If the husband is unable to pay, the son is instructed to lend her the necessary funds and can later recover from the husband when he becomes solvent. If the son refuses, the qadi can compel him to pay directly, viewing the insolvent husband as deceased for this purpose. The Hanafi position here emphasizes the primary responsibility of the husband and the subsidiary role of children.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Financial maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears her master's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a son obliged to provide maintenance for his mother?
A) Always, regardless of her marital status
B) When she is not married or her husband is insolvent
C) Only if she is divorced
D) Only if she is a widow

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a son is not required to support his father's wife, but must maintain his mother if she lacks a solvent husband.

Basis of Maintenance: Closeness vs. Inheritance – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the basis of maintenance obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that maintenance is based on closeness and filiation, and explain the conflicting narrations regarding inheritance as a factor.

Core Idea
Maintenance is based on closeness and filiation, not inheritance, unless closeness is equal – then inheritance determines apportionment.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: should maintenance for parents and children be determined by closeness of relationship or by inheritance shares? The author asserts that closeness and filiation are paramount, yet numerous branches in the text appear to consider inheritance. The commentator weaves through these contradictions, offering a resolution in a separate treatise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Principle
Locate the author's statement that maintenance is based on closeness (qurb) and filiation (juz'iyya), not inheritance.
Found in the beginning: 'إنما هو القرب والجزئية ولا يعتبر الميراث'.
2
Examine the Supporting Examples
Review the examples where closeness overrides inheritance: e.g., son over grandson, daughter over sister, daughter's child over son's son.
These illustrate the general rule.
3
Spot the Contradictions
Identify the branches where maintenance is apportioned according to inheritance, such as grandfather+grandson, mother+uncle, etc.
These appear to contradict the stated principle.
4
Understand the Commentator's Response
Notice that the commentator acknowledges the existence of narrations that consider inheritance, but the relied-upon texts (Wiqqayah, Multaqa, Tanwir) uphold closeness. He promises a separate treatise for a full resolution.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a settled matter.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Determine the practical difference: e.g., if a poor person has a daughter and a grandson, under closeness the daughter pays; under inheritance the grandson might pay a share.
The mufta bihi view is closeness, but the alternative must be known.

And the author indicated by his saying 'and for his parents' that the consideration in the obligation of maintenance for parents and children is only closeness and filiation, and inheritance is not considered. They said: If they are equal in closeness, it is obligatory on the one who has some preponderance. If neither has preponderance, then maintenance is obligatory in proportion to inheritance. So if a poor person has a son and a grandson (son's son) both wealthy, maintenance is on the son because he is closer. If he has a daughter and a grandson, maintenance is on the daughter alone, even if inheritance is between them. His saying: (only closeness and filiation) accordingly, if he has a son's daughter or daughter's daughter and a son's son, maintenance is on the daughter's child even if inheritance is for the son's grandson, and he stated it clearly. And his saying 'obligatory on the one who has some preponderance' means like a son's son and a daughter's daughter, it is on the son's son due to his preponderance (that he is the heir), but this branch needs a text from their words, otherwise it contradicts what follows shortly from branches indicating that inheritance is not considered at all in maintenance of ascendants on descendants. He said in Ahkam al-Sighar: If he has a daughter's daughter and a son's daughter both wealthy and a wealthy brother, maintenance is on his grandchild because in the chapter of maintenance the closest is considered, and inheritance is not considered in children. And he said after it also: His maintenance is on the children of daughters, male and female equal, and inheritance is not considered in children; only closeness is considered, so if he has a daughter and a son's son, maintenance is on the daughter. His saying: (inheritance is not considered) contradicts what will come before his saying: and it is valid to sell the property of his son, for he has a mother and a wealthy uncle, maintenance is on both in thirds. For him a mother and two fathers, similarly, the mother is closer than the grandfather. And similarly it contradicts his saying shortly: If he has a grandfather and a son's son, maintenance is on both according to their inheritance. And also what we will mention shortly: his saying: (in proportion to inheritance) is objected by the son and daughter, for there is no preponderance between them; maintenance is equal on them. His saying: (then maintenance is on the daughter's child) is: with difference of religion only by marriage and birth, and the father and son do not participate in the maintenance of his child with... because the daughter is closer. And if he has a daughter's daughter or a son's daughter and a brother by father and mother, maintenance is on the daughter's child, male or female, even if inheritance is for the brother not for the daughter's child. And if he has a father and a child both wealthy, maintenance is on his child, even if they are equal in closeness, due to the preponderance of the child by the interpretation 'you and your property belong to your father'. And if he has a grandfather and a son's son, maintenance is on both according to their inheritance: on the grandfather one sixth and the rest on the son's son. The evidence for not considering inheritance in this maintenance is that if one of them is a dhimmi, maintenance is on both even though inheritance is for the Muslim of them. And if a poor Muslim has a Christian son and a Muslim brother, maintenance is on the son and inheritance is for the brother. And if a poor person has a daughter and a patron of emancipation both wealthy, maintenance is on the daughter even if they are equal in inheritance; as in al-Dhakhira. And the author made the grandfather absolute, including father's father and mother's father. It is confirmed in al-Dhakhira and others, and the difference regarding mother's father is narrated. And he made the grandmother absolute, including grandmother from father's side and grandmother from mother's side. In al-Walwaljiyya: If the father takes the prescribed maintenance and clothing in advance and that is lost, another is prescribed for him. If the period passes and it remains, another is not prescribed, unlike the wife in both cases, and we have mentioned the difference in the beginning of the chapter of maintenance. His saying: (and it is not obligatory with difference of religion except by marriage and birth) as for marriage, for what we mentioned that it is because he is a part, even if they are equal in closeness as in al-Qahistani, and this indicates that preponderance in his saying 'even if they are equal in closeness' includes filiation. His saying: (then maintenance is on both...) He said in al-Bada'i: Because they are equal in closeness and inheritance, and no preponderance for one over the other from another aspect, so maintenance is on both according to inheritance. Then he said in al-Bada'i also: Likewise, if he has a mother and a brother by father and mother or by father, or a nephew by father and mother or by father, or an uncle by father and mother or by father, maintenance is on both in thirds: one third on the mother, two thirds on the brother, nephew, or uncle. I say: All these branches are problematic for their consideration of closeness and filiation without inheritance, for they have considered inheritance without closeness and filiation, since the requirement of their mentioned principle is that maintenance is only on the mother, unless this is according to the other narration that considers inheritance, as al-Qahistani attributed to the Imam, where he said: Closeness and filiation are considered, inheritance is not considered, as is a narration from him. But the narration of considering closeness and filiation is what the texts like al-Wiqayah, al-Multaqa, and al-Tanwir are upon. Then the answer to these objections appeared to me completely, and I wrote the issue with a research I was not preceded in, in a treatise called Tahrir al-Nuqul fi Nafaqat al-Furu' wa al-Usul, which every jurist must seek, for it removes ambiguity and eliminates all conjecture. His saying: (the evidence for not considering inheritance...) He said in al-Bada'i: If he has a daughter and a sister, maintenance is on the daughter because of birth, and this indicates that maintenance is not based on inheritance because the sister inherits with the daughter but has no maintenance with the daughter. This branch has also been mentioned in al-Dhakhira, but the author omitted it for brevity. His saying: (and he made the grandfather absolute...) He said in al-Dhakhira: Regarding the grandfather, poverty is considered for his entitlement to maintenance, as is the apparent narration, as in the case of the father, and the grandfather from the mother's side is like the grandfather from the father's side, and what is considered for grandfathers is also considered for grandmothers.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the basis for maintenance obligations among ascendants and descendants. The core principle, stated by the author (al-Haskafi in al-Durr al-Mukhtar or similar), is that maintenance for parents and children is based on closeness of relationship (qurb) and filiation (juz'iyya), not on inheritance shares. The commentator (al-Haskafi or Ibn Abidin) explains this principle and provides numerous examples. For instance, a poor person's maintenance is on his son, not his grandson, because the son is closer. However, the passage also presents many cases where maintenance is apportioned according to inheritance shares, such as when the grandfather and grandson are both liable, maintenance is divided as per inheritance (1/6 and 5/6). This creates a contradiction, leading to a dispute within the Hanafi school. Some narrations from Abu Hanifa consider inheritance, while the relied-upon texts (al-Wiqayah, al-Multaqa) uphold closeness and filiation. The commentator resolves the contradiction by stating he has written a separate treatise clarifying the issue. The passage also discusses the effect of difference of religion: maintenance between relatives of different faiths is only obligatory through marriage or birth, not through mere kinship. This is evidenced by the case where a Muslim and a dhimmi both owe maintenance, despite inheritance going to the Muslim.

Key Terms
قرب (qurb): Closeness of blood relation in the family tree, used to determine who is most responsible for maintenance.
جزئية (juz'iyya): Filiation, the fact of being a part or descendant of a person, emphasizing direct parent-child relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle stated in the passage, if a poor person has a daughter and a sister (both wealthy), who is primarily responsible for maintenance?
A) The daughter, because she is closer
B) The sister, because she is a sibling
C) Both equally, because they both inherit
D) The sister, because she is an heir

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, maintenance among ascendants and descendants is primarily based on closeness of relation, not inheritance, though inheritance may be considered when closeness is equal.
